Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Takbir and Its Substitutes in Prayer
Ruling on the opening takbir and its substitutes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on valid substitutes for the opening takbir, explain the Quranic proof, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools.

Core Idea
Any word of glorification in any language suffices for the opening takbir, though the standard takbir is preferred.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is the essential entry into prayer. While the standard phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the norm, the Hanafi school recognizes that the essence of takbir is glorification of Allah. Thus, substitutes like tasbih (Subhan Allah), tahlil (La ilaha illa Allah), or even foreign-language equivalents are valid, especially for those unable to speak Arabic. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the Quranic proof, and the scholarly disagreements surrounding this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
State what the opening takbir is and its legal status (wajib). Recognize that substitutes are permissible but makruh.
The passage treats the takbir as the standard, but allows alternatives.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited (Surah al-A'la 87:15) and understand its relevance to the takbir.
The verse mentions 'remembrance of the Lord' in the context of prayer.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse supports the permissibility of any glorification. The key point: the verse uses absolute (mutlaq) remembrance, so any word of glorification qualifies.
This is the core of the Hanafi argument.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that Abu Yusuf restricts substitutes to specific Arabic forms, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow any language.
The text states that the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is adopted.
5
Compare with other schools
Recognize that Shafi'i and Maliki restrict the takbir to Arabic only, and understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
For example, a Persian speaker's prayer is valid in Hanafi but invalid in Shafi'i.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة فصل في كيفية الصلاة فصل زك ف س ك ف ط و وإذا أراد الدخول في الصلاة كبر ورفع يديه حذاء أذنيه، ولو شرع بالتسبيح أي المصلي س ك ف و أي صلاة كانت ف و أو التهليل أو بالفارسية صح كما لو قرأ بها عاجزاً . من بأن قال: لا إله إلا الله خبر فصل: [ أي في كيفية تركيب أفعال الصلاة] هو لغة: الحاجز، وعرفاً طائفة من المسائل داخلة تحت كتاب، وهو مصدر يحتمل أن يكون بمعنى الفاعل كرجل عدل أي فاصل بين ما ذكر قبله ، وبعده، ويحتمل أن يكون بمعنى المفعول، والمعنى هذا مفصول عما قبله فإن ذكرت بعده "في" يرفع وينون على أنه مبتدأ محذوف أي هذا فصل، وإن لم تذكر بعده "في" سكن آخره؛ لأنك إذا وقفت على كلمة سكنت آخرها، والأحكام المذكورة في هذا الفصل مشتركة بين المصلين والمختص بالمقتدي أن يحاذي تكبيره تكبير ،إمامه وأنه أفضل عنده، وعندهما: يوصله بتكبيره أي يوصل ألف "الله" براء "أكبر"، ولا تدرك فضيلة التحريمة عنده إلا بالمحاذاة، وعندهما إلى الفراغ الثناء في الأصح. (فتح) كبر أي قال: الله أكبر، وإذا حذف المصلي أو الحالف أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة أو حذف الهاء اختلف في صحة تحريمته وانعقاد يمينه وحل ذبيحته، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً. (فتح) إلا إذا كان أخرس أو أمياً لا يحسن شيئاً فدخولهما بالنية فقط، ولا يلزمهما تحريك اللسان. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٦/١] ورفع يديه: [مقدما على التكبير وعند أبي يوسف مقارنا معه، قوله: "حذاء أذنيه" والأمة كالرجل، والحرة ترفع حذاء منكبيها، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد في حق الرجل عيني طائي وكيفيته أن يرفع يديه حتى يحاذي بإلهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، وبرؤوس الأصابع فروع أذنيه، وقال الشافعي حذاء منكبيه؛ لأنه وأصحابه كانوا يرفعون إلى المناكب، ولنا حديث وائل بن حجر أنه علي كان إذا كبر يرفع يديه حذاء أذنيه، وما رواه محمول على حالة العذر؛ لأن وائلاً قال: ثم أتيت من العام المقبل وعليهم الأكسية والبرانس، فكانوا يرفعون فيها إلى مناكبهم، فعلم أن ذلك كان لعذر البرد. (فتح) بالتسبيح بأن قال: "سبحان الله" عوض "الله أكبر". بالفارسية [ أي غير العربية من أي لسان كان] أي مطلقاً . صح عنده، وعن أبي يوسف: إن كان ويعرف أن الشروع يفتتح به لا يصير شارعاً إلا بقوله: الله أكبر أو الله الأكبر أو الله كبير أو الله الكبير؛ لأنه قد جاء في كلامهم أفعل بمعنى فعيل وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز إلا "الله أكبر أو الله الأكبر"، وعند مالك إلا بـ "الله أكبر"، . وعند الإمام ومحمد يجوز بكل ما يدل على التعظيم سواء كان بالعربية أو الفارسية والعبرانية أو الهندية وغيرها، لهما: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى الله (الأعلى: ١٥) نزلت في تكبيرة الافتتاح، فقد اعتبر مطلق بے يحسن التكبير الذكر، والمقصود التعظيم وقد حصل، ولكن قيل : يكره الشروع بغير لفظ التكبير لأجل الأخبار. (فتح) كما لو قرأ إلخ: أي صح بالتسبيح والتهليل بالفارسية كما يصح لو قرأ بالفارسية عاجزا عن العربية، وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز بلا عجز أيضا، وقال الشافعي: لا تجوز القراءة بالفارسية أصلاً، لكنه إن كان لا يحسن العربية فهو يصلي بغير قراءة حتى لو قرأ بالفارسية تفسد عنده. (فتح) أو ذبح وسمى بها، لا بـ"اللهم اغفر لي"، وسمى بها : أي بالفارسية جاز أيضاً بلا خلاف وكذا التلبية في الحج والسلام. (عيني) لا بـ اللهم إلخ: لأنه ليس بتعظيم خالص؛ إذ هو مشوب بحاجته، ولو أبدل "الكاف" من أكبر "قافاً" يصير شارعاً؛ لأن العرب تفعله. (عيني)
The Book of Prayer. A chapter on the manner of prayer. A section. When a person intends to enter prayer, he says the takbir and raises his hands to his ears. If he begins with tasbih or tahlil or Persian, it is valid, just as it is valid if he recites in Persian when unable (to recite in Arabic). ... (Follows the text as in arabic_clean with literal rendering)
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof that states the required opening of prayer. The takbir 'Allahu Akbar' is the standard, but substitutes such as saying 'Subhan Allah' or 'La ilaha illa Allah' or any phrase in Persian or other languages are valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf restricts it to specific Arabic forms. The Hanafi school relies on the Quranic verse (al-A'la 15) which mentions remembering the Lord. However, they declare it makruh to use non-standard wording due to prophetic practice. The passage also discusses raising hands to the ears for men, contrasting with Shafi'i who raises to shoulders, and provides a hadith from Wail ibn Hujr. The ruling extends to slaughtering and saying Bismillah in Persian, but not to supplications like 'Allahumma ighfir li' as they lack pure glorification.

Key Terms
التكبيرة الأولى (at-takbirat al-ula): The opening takbir that initiates prayer, also called takbirat al-ihram.
التسبيح (at-tasbih): Saying 'Subhan Allah' as a substitute for the opening takbir.
الفارسية (al-farisiyyah): The Persian language; considered a valid substitute for the takbir in case of inability or even without inability according to Abu Hanifa.
التهليل (at-tahlil): Saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' as a substitute for the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following phrases can validly replace the opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) for a non-Arabic speaker?
A) Subhan Allah
B) Allahumma ighfir li
C) La ilaha illa Allah
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the opening takbir is wajib but can be substituted by any word of glorification in any language, though the standard Arabic takbir is superior and preferred.

The Opening Du'a and Ta'awwudh: Hanafi Ruling and Maliki Dispute
Ruling on reciting thana and ta'awwudh quietly in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on thana and ta'awwudh in prayer, identify when a follower omits thana, and evaluate the Maliki objection and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, the imam and follower recite thana and ta'awwudh silently; the follower only omits thana if the imam has begun recitation.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on reciting the opening supplication (thana) and the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. The text discusses whether the imam and follower recite these, and under what conditions a latecomer may omit thana. We also explore the Maliki school's objection and the Hanafi response, learning how the schools reconcile conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification of thana and ta'awwudh: are they fard, wajib, or sunnah? Note that Hanafi considers them sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
The hukm level affects the consequence of omission: omission is not sinful but loses reward.
2
State the Hanafi position
Who recites thana and ta'awwudh? The imam and follower both recite them silently, except that the follower omits thana if the imam has already started recitation.
The text mentions exceptions for latecomers (masbuq).
3
Detail the latecomer's rules
According to al-Sharnablaliyah, if a latecomer catches the imam in ruku', he says takbir while standing and goes straight into ruku', leaving thana. If he catches the imam in sujud or sitting, he recites thana after his own takbir before joining.
The ruling covers both jama'ah and masbuq scenarios.
4
Examine the Maliki objection
Malik's proof: Hadith of Anas that the Prophet and the caliphs began prayer with 'Al-hamdu lillah' or 'Umm al-Quran', implying no thana or ta'awwudh.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different hadiths.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Hanafi reconciles by interpreting 'prayer' in that hadith as referring only to the recitation of al-Fatihah, not the entire prayer. The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri explicitly shows the Prophet using ta'awwudh after the opening takbir.
The Hanafi position is supported by explicit evidence and contextual interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستفتحاً: حال من المستكن في "وضع وشامل للإمام والمأموم، إلا إذا شرع الإمام في القراءة، مسبوقاً كان أو مدركا جهر الإمام أو لا، وفي الشرنبلالية: أدرك الإمام في الركوع يحرم قائما ويركع ويترك الثناء، وإن أدركه في السجود يأتي به بعد التحريمة ويسجد، وكذا لو أدركه في القعدة. (فتح) وتعوذ سرا: مطلقاً سواء كان إماماً أو منفرداً، وقال مالك: لا يأتي الإمام بالتعوذ ولا بالثناء؛ لحديث أنس له : كنا نصلي خلف رسول الله وأبي بكر الله وعمر الله وعثمان الله فكانوا يستفتحون الصلاة بـ"الحمد رب العالمين"، وفي رواية بـ " أم القرآن، ولنا حديث أبي سعيد الخدري أن النبي كان إذا قام إلى الصلاة استفتح ثم يقول: أعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم والمراد بالصلاة فيما رواه قراءة الفاتحة كما في حديث آخر "قسمت الصلاة بيني وبين عبدي نصفين"، فإن المراد ههنا قراءة الفاتحة. (فتح)
Mastaftihan: A circumstantial modifier for the hidden subject in 'place' and includes the imam and the follower, except when the imam begins recitation, whether the follower is preceded or catches up, whether the imam recites aloud or not. In al-Sharnablaliyah: If he catches the imam in ruku', he says the takbir while standing and bows and leaves the thana. If he catches him in prostration, he recites it after the takbir and prostrates, likewise if he catches him in the sitting. (Fath) And he seeks refuge quietly: absolutely, whether he is imam or alone. Malik said: The imam does not recite the ta'awwudh nor the thana due to the hadith of Anas: 'We used to pray behind the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they would open prayer with 'Al-hamdu lillahi rabbil alamin' and in another narration with 'Umm al-Quran.' Our proof is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet, when he stood for prayer, would open then say: 'I seek refuge in Allah, the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing, from the accursed Satan.' And the intended meaning of 'prayer' in what he narrated is the recitation of al-Fatihah, as in another hadith: 'I have divided the prayer between Me and My servant into two halves,' here the intended meaning is the recitation of al-Fatihah. (Fath)
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the recitation of the opening supplication (thana) and the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. The Hanafi position is that both are recited silently by the imam and follower, except the follower must omit thana if he joins after the imam has started reciting. The text explains detailed rules from al-Sharnablaliyah for a latecomer. Malik held that the imam should not recite thana or ta'awwudh at all, based on a hadith that the Prophet and the caliphs began prayer directly with 'Al-hamdu lillah'. The Hanafi response reconciles the hadith by arguing that 'prayer' in that context refers to the Fatihah recitation, not the entire prayer, and cites a hadith where the Prophet used ta'awwudh after the opening. Thus, the Hanafi school requires these silent recitations for imam and alone worshipper, but the follower omits thana when the imam recites.

Key Terms
الاستفتاح (al-istiftah): The opening supplication (thana) recited after takbirat al-ihram, e.g., 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'.
التعوذ (at-ta'awwudh): Saying 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim' before reciting al-Fatihah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a latecomer (masbuq) omit the opening supplication (thana)?
A) When he joins the imam in ruku'
B) When he joins the imam in sujud
C) When he joins the imam in the sitting position
D) He never omits it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates silent recitation of thana and ta'awwudh for imam and follower, with specific exceptions for latecomers based on timing.

Hand Placement in Prayer: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Detailed Hanafi ruling on the Sunnah of placing right hand on left under the navel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in prayer, distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and explain the evidence and practical consequences of each.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left under the navel is Sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage examines one of the most visible differences between the schools: where and how to place the hands during prayer. The Hanafi school holds it as a confirmed Sunnah to place the right palm on the left palm under the navel, while Shafi'i places on the chest and Malik considers letting the hands hang superior. The text not only gives the Hanafi view but also provides a systematic four-aspect analysis and rebuttals to the opposing schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling (Sunnah), the method (palm on palm, thumb and little finger around wrist), the location (under navel), and the timing (immediately after takbir per zahir al-riwaya).
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: Muhammad places during recitation only; the relied-upon view places right after takbir.
2
Identify the opponents and their views
Two opponents: Malik says letting hands hang is better (placing is a concession); Shafi'i says placing on the chest is Sunnah.
Malik's evidence is the practice of the Prophet and Companions whose blood dripped on their fingertips, implying normal posture was hanging.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Shafi'i cites Quran 108:2 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' interpreting 'sacrifice' (nahr) as placing hands on the upper chest. Malik relies on the reported practice of the Companions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi rebuts Shafi'i: the verse refers to animal sacrifice, not hand placement. Hanafi rebuts Malik: the blood-dripping evidence indicates injury, not normal posture. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'It is from the Sunnah to place the right on the left under the navel.'
The Hanafi position is also supported by the hadith 'We were commanded to take our left arms with our right hands in prayer.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects the actual posture during prayer: Hanafi hands under navel, Shafi'i on chest, Maliki hands hanging. This is visible in congregational prayers and is a distinguishing feature of each school.
The Hanafi method combining palm on palm and wrist grasp satisfies both 'taking' and 'placing' hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووضع يمينه على يساره تحت السرة بالفارسية مستفتحاً، وتعوذ سرا أي قائلا سبحانك اللهم إلخ أي كف يمينه وسمى بها : أي بالفارسية جاز أيضاً بلا خلاف وكذا التلبية في الحج والسلام. (عيني) لا بـ اللهم إلخ: لأنه ليس بتعظيم خالص؛ إذ هو مشوب بحاجته، ولو أبدل "الكاف" من أكبر "قافاً" يصير شارعاً؛ لأن العرب تفعله. (عيني) ووضع يمينه: أي الوضع سنة قيام حقيقة أو حكماً، كما إذا صلى قاعداً فيه ذكر مسنون طويل عندهما، وعند محمد سنة قيام فيه قراءة، فيعتمد عندهما في حالة الثناء والقنوت وصلاة الجنازة، وعند محمد يرسل فيها، وأما في القومة التي بين الركوع والسجود وبين تكبيرات العيدين فيرسل اتفاقاً. (فتح) على يساره [يعني الكف على الكف، ويقال على المفصل، وعند أبي يوسف يأخذ رسغ يده اليسرى بالخنصر والإبهام، وهو المختار الكلام في وضع اليمين من أربعة أوجه الأول: أن الوضع سنة أم لا، والثاني: صفة الوضع، والثالث: موضع الوضع والرابع: متى يضع. أما الأول : فعند علمائنا الوضع سنة، وقال مالك: الفضيلة في الإرسال والرخصة في الأخذ؛ لأن النبي عليه كان يفعل كذلك وكذا الصحابة حتى نزلت الدم على رؤوس أصابعهم، ولنا: حديث عليه "إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة في الصلاة." وأما صفة الوضع، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ وهو قوله عليه: "نحن - معشر الأنبياء – أمرنا أن نأخذ شمائلنا بأيماننا في الصلاة"، وفي حديث علي الله الله الوضع كما مر ، واستحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه الأيمن على ظهر كفه الأيسر، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ ليكون عاملاً بالحديثين، وأما موضع الوضع فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، وعند الشافعي على الصدر؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرْ (الكوثر : ٢) المراد وضع اليمين على الشمال على النحر، وهو الصدر، وما روينا من الحديثين حجة عليه في الوضع، وعلى مالك في الإرسال، والمراد من الآية نحر الأضحية، وأما متى يضع؟ فعند محمد عند القراءة، وفي ظاهر الرواية: يضع كما يرفع يديه بعد التكبير فيعتمد. (مستخلص)
And he places his right hand on his left under the navel... (Then commentary:) Placing the right hand: it is Sunnah for one who is standing in reality or by legal fiction, such as when praying sitting, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it contains a long recommended remembrance, and according to Muhammad it is Sunnah for standing in which there is recitation, so according to the two he leans (places hands) in the state of thana, qunut, and funeral prayer, and according to Muhammad he lets them hang therein. As for the standing between bowing and prostration and between the takbirs of the two Eids, he lets them hang by agreement. (Fath) On his left [meaning palm on palm, and it is said on the joint, and according to Abu Yusuf he takes the wrist of his left hand with the little finger and thumb, and that is the chosen. The discussion on placing the right hand consists of four aspects: first, whether the placing is Sunnah or not; second, the description of the placement; third, the location of the placement; fourth, when to place. As for the first: according to our scholars, the placement is Sunnah. Malik said: Virtue is in letting the hands hang, and permission is in taking, because the Prophet did that and so did the Companions until blood dripped on their fingertips. Our proof: the hadith 'It is from the Sunnah to place the right hand on the left under the navel in prayer.' As for the description of the placement: in the marfu' hadith is the word 'taking' which is his statement: 'We, the company of Prophets, were commanded to take our left arms with our right hands in prayer.' In the hadith of Ali is 'placing' as mentioned. Many of our scholars recommended combining both by placing the inner palm of the right hand on the back of the left palm and encircling the wrist with the little finger and thumb, to act on both hadiths. As for the location: the best in our view is under the navel. Shafi'i said: on the chest based on the verse 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (Kawthar 2); he intended placing the right on the left on the nahr (upper chest). Our hadiths are evidence against him in placing, and against Malik in letting hang. The intended meaning of the verse is the sacrifice of the udhiyah. As for when to place: according to Muhammad, at the time of recitation; in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), he places right after raising his hands after the takbir and then relies. (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi ruling on placing the right hand on the left during prayer. It begins with the statement that the hand is placed under the navel. The commentary (Fath) explains that placing is Sunnah for the standing position, but there is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is Sunnah for standing that involves long recitation (like thana, qunut, funeral prayer), whereas according to Muhammad alone, it is Sunnah for any standing that includes recitation (like during al-Fatihah). In positions where there is no recitation (between bowing and prostrating, between Eid takbirs), the hands are left hanging by consensus. The text then organizes the discussion into four aspects: (1) whether placing is Sunnah or not – Hanafi says it is Sunnah, Malik says it is only a concession and the better act is to let them hang. Hanafi cites a hadith stating it is from the Sunnah to place under the navel. (2) The manner – the preferred method combines placing the palm on the palm and grasping the wrist with the thumb and little finger to satisfy both hadiths about 'taking' and 'placing'. (3) The location – under the navel, against Shafi'i who says on the chest using verse 2 of al-Kawthar. Hanafi responds that the verse refers to slaughtering for sacrifice, not hand placement. (4) Timing – according to Muhammad, at the time of recitation; in the zahir al-riwaya (the relied-upon position), immediately after the opening takbir before recitation.

Key Terms
الوضع (al-wad): Placing the right hand on the left during prayer (qiyam).
الإرسال (al-irsal): Letting the hands hang loosely at the sides during prayer.
النحر (al-nahr): The upper part of the chest, near the neck. Used by Shafi'i to denote the recommended hand placement location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which praying positions are the hands left hanging by agreement (ittiqaq)?
A) During the opening thana and qunut
B) During the standing between bowing and prostration (qawma) and between Eid takbirs
C) During the funeral prayer and in sujud
D) During the recitation of al-Fatihah and after the surah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that placing the right hand on the left under the navel after takbir is a confirmed Sunnah, supported by explicit hadith, with a combined method that reconciles both 'taking' and 'placing' narrations.

The Ruling on Hand Placement: Sunna or Not?
Hanafi ruling with proof on the sunna status of hand placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing the right hand on the left in prayer, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain why the Hanafis consider it sunna while Malik considered letting hang superior.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left is sunna mu'akkada, not fard — the hadith says 'min al-sunna'.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the first of four aspects: whether the placement is sunna or not. The Hanafi school holds it is sunna, based on a clear hadith. Imam Malik took a different view, citing the practice of the Prophet and Companions who let their hands hang. In this lesson, you will examine the evidence and see why the Hanafi position is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is placing the right hand on the left during standing in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunna (recommended), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The hadith 'Inna min al-sunnati wad' al-yamin 'ala al-shimal tahta al-surra fi al-salah' explicitly calls it sunna.
3
Understand the opposing Maliki proof
The practice of the Prophet and Companions letting hands hang, to the point blood dripped from their fingertips.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi response is that the hadith is explicit and the Companions' practice was due to hardship; the Hanafi position is more sound based on direct textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووضع يمينه على يساره تحت السرة أي كف يمينه، ووضع يمينه: أي الوضع سنة قيام حقيقة أو حكماً، كما إذا صلى قاعداً فيه ذكر مسنون طويل عندهما، وعند محمد سنة قيام فيه قراءة، فيعتمد عندهما في حالة الثناء والقنوت وصلاة الجنازة، وعند محمد يرسل فيها، وأما في القومة التي بين الركوع والسجود وبين تكبيرات العيدين فيرسل اتفاقاً. (فتح) على يساره [يعني الكف على الكف، ويقال على المفصل، وعند أبي يوسف يأخذ رسغ يده اليسرى بالخنصر والإبهام، وهو المختار الكلام في وضع اليمين من أربعة أوجه الأول: أن الوضع سنة أم لا، والثاني: صفة الوضع، والثالث: موضع الوضع والرابع: متى يضع. أما الأول : فعند علمائنا الوضع سنة، وقال مالك: الفضيلة في الإرسال والرخصة في الأخذ؛ لأن النبي عليه كان يفعل كذلك وكذا الصحابة حتى نزلت الدم على رؤوس أصابعهم، ولنا: حديث عليه "إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة في الصلاة." وأما صفة الوضع، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ وهو قوله عليه: "نحن - معشر الأنبياء – أمرنا أن نأخذ شمائلنا بأيماننا في الصلاة"، وفي حديث علي الله الله الوضع كما مر ، واستحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه الأيمن على ظهر كفه الأيسر، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ ليكون عاملاً بالحديثين، وأما موضع الوضع فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، وعند الشافعي على الصدر؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرْ (الكوثر : ٢) المراد وضع اليمين على الشمال على النحر، وهو الصدر، وما روينا من الحديثين حجة عليه في الوضع، وعلى مالك في الإرسال، والمراد من الآية نحر الأضحية، وأما متى يضع؟ فعند محمد عند القراءة، وفي ظاهر الرواية: يضع كما يرفع يديه بعد التكبير فيعتمد. (مستخلص)
And he places his right hand on his left under the navel – meaning the palm of his right hand. And the placing of his right hand: It is sunna while standing, actually or effectively, as if he prays sitting and there is a lengthy supererogatory dhikr according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to Muhammad it is sunna while standing with recitation. So he supports (his hands) according to them during thana', qunoot, and funeral prayer, while according to Muhammad he lets them hang. As for the standing between bowing and prostration and between 'Eid takbeers, he lets them hang by agreement. (Fath) On his left [meaning palm on palm, and it is said on the joint. According to Abu Yusuf, he grips the left wrist with the little finger and thumb, and that is the chosen view. The discussion on placing the right hand is from four aspects: first, whether the placing is sunna or not; second, the description of the placing; third, the place of placing; fourth, when to place. As for the first: According to our scholars, the placing is sunna. Malik said: Virtue is in letting hang, and license in holding; because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do that, and so did the Companions, to the point that blood dripped from their fingertips. Our evidence: a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'It is from the sunna to place the right hand on the left under the navel in prayer.' As for the description of the placing: In the marfoo' hadith is the wording 'grasping' – his statement: 'We, the company of prophets, were commanded to grasp our left hands with our right in prayer.' In the hadith of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is 'placing' as mentioned. Many of our mashayikh considered it commendable to combine both: he places the inner palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand and encircles with the little finger and thumb around the wrist, so as to act upon both hadiths. As for the place of placing: According to us, the best is under the navel. According to al-Shafi'i, it is on the chest due to His statement: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (al-Kawthar 2) – meaning placing the right hand on the left on the chest. What we have narrated from the two hadiths is evidence against him regarding the place, and against Malik regarding letting hang. The intended meaning of the verse is sacrificing the udhiya. As for when he places? According to Muhammad, at the time of recitation. In the zahir al-riwaya, he places as he raises his hands after the takbeer and then relies. (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi ruling with proof regarding the placement of the right hand on the left during prayer. The matn states that one places his right hand on his left under the navel. The commentary expands on four aspects: 1) Ruling: It is sunna according to the Hanafis, while Imam Malik considered letting the hands hang as superior. The Hanafi proof is a hadith stating it is from the sunna to place the right hand on the left under the navel. 2) Description: There are two transmitted ways – 'placing' (from a hadith of 'Ali) and 'grasping' (from a hadith of the Prophet). Many Hanafi scholars combine them by placing the palm on the back of the left hand and gripping the wrist with the little finger and thumb. 3) Location: The best position is under the navel (Hanafi) as opposed to the chest (Shafi'i), who interprets the verse of sacrifice as pointing to the chest. The Hanafis argue the verse refers to actual sacrifice. 4) Timing: According to Imam Muhammad, the hands are placed at the start of recitation; the zahir al-riwaya states it is at the lift of hands after takbeer. The text also notes exceptions for bowing and 'Eid takbeers where hands are left hanging by agreement.

Key Terms
وضع اليمين على اليسار (wad' al-yamin 'ala al-shimal): The act of placing the right hand on the left during standing in prayer.
السنة (al-sunna): In this context, a recommended act (mustahab) that is regularly performed by the Prophet; omission does not require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited by the Hanafis, where should the right hand be placed?
A) On the chest
B) Under the navel
C) On the left shoulder
D) Letting hang

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that placing the right hand on the left under the navel is a sunna mu'akkada, supported by explicit hadith, and it is not obligatory.

The Details of Hand Placement: Description, Location, and Timing
Hanafi expansion on the manner, place, and timing of hand placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of placing the right hand on the left, state the preferred location (under navel vs chest), and identify the timing differences within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school combines two hadiths: place the palm on the back of the left hand and grip the wrist with the little finger and thumb, under the navel, after the takbeer.

After establishing that the hand placement is sunna, the passage delves into three more aspects: the exact description, the best location, and the timing. There are differences even within the Hanafi school on how to do it and when. In this lesson, you will learn the details that distinguish the Hanafi practice from others.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two transmitted descriptions
One hadith mentions 'placing' (wad') from 'Ali; another mentions 'grasping' (akhdh) from the Prophet. These are not contradictory but complementary.
2
See how the Hanafis combine them
Many mashayikh combine: place the inner palm of the right on the back of the left, and encircle the wrist with the little finger and thumb. This acts on both hadiths.
3
Identify the location dispute
Hanafis say under the navel; Shafi'is say on the chest based on the verse 'fasalli li-rabbika wanhar'. The Hanafis argue the verse refers to actual sacrifice.
4
Know the timing
Imam Muhammad says at the start of recitation; the zahir al-riwaya says after the takbeer. The latter is more widely adopted.
5
Note the exceptions
During ruku', between sajdahs, and during 'Eid takbeers, the hands are left hanging by agreement.

The Opening Supplication (Thana') and Seeking Refuge (Ta'awwudh) in Prayer: Rulings and Proofs
Ruling on thana' and ta'awwudh with proof and Maliki objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (sunnah) for thana' and ta'awwudh in prayer, identify the proofs from hadith and Quran, and explain why the Hanafi school holds that the imam and munfarid recite them quietly.

Core Idea
Thana' and ta'awwudh are sunnah in prayer; the evidence links ta'awwudh to recitation, establishing its place at the start of qira'a.

In this lesson, we examine the opening supplication (thana') and seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in the Hanafi school. These are part of the prayer's sunan, not fard or wajib. We will look at the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and the difference with the Maliki school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is thana' (opening supplication) and ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). The ruling is sunnah for imam and munfarid, recited quietly.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) would open with thana' and then say 'A'udhu...'. Also, Quran 16:98 commands seeking refuge when reciting Quran.
The verse is used to link ta'awwudh to recitation, not to thana'.
3
Understand the Hanafi interpretation
The Quranic command 'When you recite the Quran, seek refuge...' is interpreted as establishing ta'awwudh's place before recitation, thus it is recited after thana' but before al-Fatiha.
4
Note the Maliki objection and Hanafi response
Malik cites the hadith of Anas that the Companions started with 'Alhamdulillah'. The Hanafi response: that hadith does not deny thana'; it shows they began with praise. The Hanafi proof is stronger.
5
State the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that thana' and ta'awwudh are sunnah for imam and munfarid, recited quietly. The imam and munfarid recite them; the muqtadi remains silent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستفتحاً: حال من المستكن في 'وضع' وشامل للإمام والمأموم، إلا إذا شرع الإمام في القراءة، مسبوقاً كان أو مدركا جهر الإمام أو لا، وفي الشرنبلالية: أدرك الإمام في الركوع يحرم قائما ويركع ويترك الثناء، وإن أدركه في السجود يأتي به بعد التحريمة ويسجد، وكذا لو أدركه في القعدة. (فتح) وتَعَوَّذْ سِرًّا: مطلقاً سواء كان إماماً أو منفرداً، وقال مالك: لا يأتي الإمام بالتعوذ ولا بالثناء؛ لحديث أنس له : كنا نصلي خلف رسول الله وأبي بكر الله وعمر الله وعثمان الله فكانوا يستفتحون الصلاة بـ'الحمد رب العالمين'، وفي رواية بـ 'أم القرآن'، ولنا حديث أبي سعيد الخدري أن النبي كان إذا قام إلى الصلاة استفتح ثم يقول: أعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم والمراد بالصلاة فيما رواه قراءة الفاتحة كما في حديث آخر 'قسمت الصلاة بيني وبين عبدي نصفين'، فإن المراد ههنا قراءة الفاتحة. (فتح) للقراءة: أي التعوذ تبع للقراءة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا قَرَأْتَ الْقُرْآنَ فَاسْتَعِذْ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ﴾ (النحل: ٩٨) أي إذا أردت قراءة القرآن كما في ﴿إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلاةِ (المائدة: ٦) أي إذا أردتم قيامها، وقال أبو يوسف: إنه تبع للثناء؛ لأن الأمر بالاستعاذة عند افتتاح القراءة لدفع الوسوسة، وهو عند افتتاح الصلاة أهم، وعند محمد هو لأجل القراءة لا لأجل الثناء عملاً بظاهر النص، وأبو حنيفة مع محمد، والمختار قول الطرفين. (فتح) فيأتي به المسبوق : [ أي التعوذ لقراءته، والمسبوق من فاته بعض ركعات الجماعة (فتح)] هذا عند الطرفين؛ لأنه لما كان تبعاً للقراءة عندهما يأتي به المسبوق؛ لأن القراءة فرض عليه، ولا يأتي به المقتدي؛ لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين؛ لأن القراءة بعدها، وعن أبي يوسف على عكس هذا فيأتي به المقتدي؛ لأنه يأتي بالثناء والتعوذ، ويأتي قبل تكبيرات العيدين؛ لأنه وقت الثناء، ولا يأتي به المسبوق؛ لأنه تعوذ حين شرع. (مستخلص) لا المقتدي لعدم قراءته، وكذا اللاحق الذي أدرك أول الصلاة مع فوات البعض من الوسط. تكبيرات العيدين: لقراءته بعدها عند محمد، وعند أبي يوسف يأتي قبل التكبيرات. (مسكين)
While opening [the prayer]: a state derived from 'places', inclusive of the imam and the follower, except when the imam has begun the recitation, whether the follower is masbuq (one who missed part) or mudrik (one who joined in time), whether he hears the imam or not. In al-Shurnublaliyya: if he catches the imam in bowing, he makes takbeer while standing and bows and leaves the thana'; if he catches him in prostration, he performs it (thana') after the opening takbeer and prostrates; similarly if he catches him in the sitting. (Fath) And he seeks refuge quietly: absolutely, whether he is imam or alone. Malik said: The imam does not recite ta'awwudh nor thana'; based on the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): We prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, 'Umar, and 'Uthman, and they used to open the prayer with 'Alhamdu lillahi rabbil 'alameen' and in another narration with 'Umm al-Quran'. Our evidence is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he stood for prayer would open then say: 'A'udhu billahi al-sami'i al-'alimi min al-shaytani al-rajim'. And what is meant by 'prayer' in what he narrated is reciting al-Fatiha, as in another hadith: 'I divided the prayer between Me and My servant into two halves' – here it means reciting al-Fatiha. (Fath) For recitation: meaning ta'awwudh is subsidiary to recitation due to His statement: 'When you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan' (al-Nahl 98) – meaning when you intend to recite the Quran, just as in 'When you stand for prayer' (al-Ma'ida 6) meaning when you intend to stand. Abu Yusuf said: It is subsidiary to thana'; because the command for seeking refuge is at the opening of recitation to repel whisperings, and it is most important at the opening of prayer. According to Muhammad, it is for the sake of recitation, not thana', acting upon the apparent text. Abu Hanifa is with Muhammad. The chosen view is the saying of both parties. (Fath) So the masbuq performs it [i.e., ta'awwudh for his recitation, and masbuq is the one who missed some rak'ahs of the congregation (Fath)] – this according to the two parties (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) ; because since ta'awwudh is subsidiary to recitation according to them, the masbuq performs it because recitation is obligatory upon him, and the muqtadi (follower) does not perform it because there is no recitation upon him. And it is delayed after the 'Eid takbeers because recitation comes after them. According to Abu Yusuf, the opposite: the muqtadi performs it because he performs thana' and ta'awwudh, and it comes before the 'Eid takbeers because it is the time of thana'; and the masbuq does not perform it because he seeks refuge when he starts (his own prayer). (Mustakhlas) Not the muqtadi due to his lack of recitation, and similarly the lahiq who caught the beginning of the prayer but missed some of the middle. The 'Eid takbeers: for recitation after them according to Muhammad; according to Abu Yusuf, it comes before the takbeers. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage deals with the opening supplication (thana') and seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer. The matn states that one opens prayer (istiftah) and seeks refuge quietly. The commentary explains that the imam and the follower (including masbuq and mudrik) should recite thana' except when the imam begins recitation. There is a hadith from Abu Sa'id that the Prophet would open with thana' and then seek refuge. The passage then discusses the nature of ta'awwudh: whether it is subsidiary to recitation (qira'a) or to thana'. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that it is for recitation (based on the verse 'When you recite the Quran...'), while Abu Yusuf says it is for thana'. The practical consequence: for the masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer), he should recite ta'awwudh because he must recite; for the muqtadi (follower), he should not because he does not recite. However, according to Abu Yusuf, the muqtadi does recite it because he recites thana'. The text also notes the timing relative to 'Eid takbeers: it is delayed after takbeers according to Muhammad (since it is before recitation), but Abu Yusuf places it before. The chosen view (mukhtar) is said to be the position of both parties (i.e., that ta'awwudh is for recitation, but thana' is separate).

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited at the start of prayer or recitation.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who misses one or more rak'ahs of the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), who should recite the ta'awwudh?
A) Only the munfarid
B) The masbuq, not the muqtadi
C) The muqtadi, not the masbuq
D) Both masbuq and muqtadi

Key Takeaway
Thana' and ta'awwudh are sunnah acts of prayer; the Hanafi school firmly bases ta'awwudh on the Quran verse linking it to recitation.

Salah — Prayer
advanced

Intra-Hanafi Difference: Who Recites Ta'awwudh?
Intra-Hanafi dispute over the basis of ta'awwudh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on ta'awwudh, and apply the correct ruling for masbuq, muqtadi, and 'Eid prayers.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad link ta'awwudh to recitation, so masbuq recites it; Abu Yusuf links it to thana', so muqtadi recites it.

Building on the general ruling, this lesson dives into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The issue is whether ta'awwudh is subsidiary to recitation or to thana'. This leads to different conclusions for who recites it in congregation and the timing in 'Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The core issue: Is ta'awwudh connected to recitation (qira'a) or to thana' (opening supplication)?
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold that ta'awwudh is subsidiary to recitation. Evidence: Quran 16:98 commands seeking refuge when reciting Quran. Thus, masbuq (who will recite) should recite ta'awwudh; muqtadi (who does not recite) should not.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that ta'awwudh is subsidiary to thana'. Reason: the need for refuge is greatest at the start of prayer. Thus, muqtadi (who recites thana') should recite ta'awwudh; masbuq (who missed thana') should not.
4
Apply to 'Eid takbeers
According to Muhammad, ta'awwudh is delayed until after the 'Eid takbeers because recitation comes after them. According to Abu Yusuf, it comes before the takbeers because it is part of thana'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The chosen view (mukhtar) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ta'awwudh is for recitation. Thus, masbuq recites it, muqtadi does not, and in 'Eid it is after the takbeers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستفتحاً: حال من المستكن في 'وضع' وشامل للإمام والمأموم، إلا إذا شرع الإمام في القراءة، مسبوقاً كان أو مدركا جهر الإمام أو لا، وفي الشرنبلالية: أدرك الإمام في الركوع يحرم قائما ويركع ويترك الثناء، وإن أدركه في السجود يأتي به بعد التحريمة ويسجد، وكذا لو أدركه في القعدة. (فتح) وتَعَوَّذْ سِرًّا: مطلقاً سواء كان إماماً أو منفرداً، وقال مالك: لا يأتي الإمام بالتعوذ ولا بالثناء؛ لحديث أنس له : كنا نصلي خلف رسول الله وأبي بكر الله وعمر الله وعثمان الله فكانوا يستفتحون الصلاة بـ'الحمد رب العالمين'، وفي رواية بـ 'أم القرآن'، ولنا حديث أبي سعيد الخدري أن النبي كان إذا قام إلى الصلاة استفتح ثم يقول: أعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم والمراد بالصلاة فيما رواه قراءة الفاتحة كما في حديث آخر 'قسمت الصلاة بيني وبين عبدي نصفين'، فإن المراد ههنا قراءة الفاتحة. (فتح) للقراءة: أي التعوذ تبع للقراءة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا قَرَأْتَ الْقُرْآنَ فَاسْتَعِذْ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ﴾ (النحل: ٩٨) أي إذا أردت قراءة القرآن كما في ﴿إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلاةِ (المائدة: ٦) أي إذا أردتم قيامها، وقال أبو يوسف: إنه تبع للثناء؛ لأن الأمر بالاستعاذة عند افتتاح القراءة لدفع الوسوسة، وهو عند افتتاح الصلاة أهم، وعند محمد هو لأجل القراءة لا لأجل الثناء عملاً بظاهر النص، وأبو حنيفة مع محمد، والمختار قول الطرفين. (فتح) فيأتي به المسبوق : [ أي التعوذ لقراءته، والمسبوق من فاته بعض ركعات الجماعة (فتح)] هذا عند الطرفين؛ لأنه لما كان تبعاً للقراءة عندهما يأتي به المسبوق؛ لأن القراءة فرض عليه، ولا يأتي به المقتدي؛ لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين؛ لأن القراءة بعدها، وعن أبي يوسف على عكس هذا فيأتي به المقتدي؛ لأنه يأتي بالثناء والتعوذ، ويأتي قبل تكبيرات العيدين؛ لأنه وقت الثناء، ولا يأتي به المسبوق؛ لأنه تعوذ حين شرع. Recitation of Basmalah in Prayer
Hanafi rulings on basmalah with disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on basmalah recitation in prayer, distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument.

Core Idea
Basmalah is recited silently in prayer; it is not part of Fatiha in the Hanafi school.

This passage examines the rulings on reciting basmalah during prayer, a point of significant dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. You will learn why the Hanafi school considers basmalah a separate opening verse recited silently, while the Shafi'i school treats it as part of Fatiha recited aloud. The text also explores internal differences within the Hanafi school regarding which rak'ahs it is recited in.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling that basmalah is recited silently and not part of Fatiha. Note the intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa recites only in first rak'ah, the two say every rak'ah.
The text also mentions the view of Muhammad on reciting basmalah between surahs as a precaution.
2
Identify the Shafi'i view and its evidence
The Shafi'i school holds that basmalah is part of Fatiha and recited aloud. Their evidence includes consensus on writing basmalah in the mushaf and hadith that the Prophet recited it aloud.
The Shafi'i also argue from the practice of 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet and caliphs did not recite basmalah aloud, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas that basmalah was revealed to separate surahs.
These hadith are considered authentic and directly address the issue.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to Shafi'i arguments
The Hanafi rebuttal: writing in the mushaf is for separation, not to indicate it is part of the surah. The hadith of reciting aloud are weak (Ibn Abd al-Barr) or can be interpreted as occasional for teaching.
This shows the importance of evaluating hadith authenticity (jarh wa ta'dil).
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis recite basmalah silently in prayer, often only in the first rak'ah; Shafi'is recite it aloud in every rak'ah before Fatiha.
This directly affects the audible recitation in congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسمى سراً : [ أي غير المؤتم بأن يقول: 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' بعد التعوذ ] روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: أنه لا يأتي بها إلا في الركعة الأولى؛ لأنها ليست من الفاتحة، وإنما هي للافتتاح، فتختص بالركعة الأولى كالتعوذ، وروى المعلى: أنه يأتي بها في كل ركعة، وهو قولهما؛ لأن التسمية وإن لم تجعل من الفاتحة قطعا، لكن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل، فصارت من الفاتحة عملاً، وأما عند رأس كل سورة فلا يأتي بها عند الشيخين، وقال محمد: يأتي بها احتياطاً، وقوله: 'سراً' أي مطلقاً، خلافاً للشافعي؛ لأنه الا الله كان يفتتح الصلاة بـ'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم'، وكان عمر وعثمان وعلي الله يجهرون بها. ولنا: ما روي عن أنس له قال : صليت خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان فلم أسمع أحداً . منهم يجهر بـ'بسم ! الله الرحمن الرحيم'، وقال أبو هريرة كان عليه لا يجهر بها، وما رواه لا دلالة فيه على الجهر، أو يحمل على أنه كان يجهر بها أحياناً للتعليم كما كان يجهر أحياناً بالقراءة في الظهر تعليماً، وما روي عن عمر وعلي وعثمان الله قال ابن عبد البر: الطرق عنهم ليست بالقوية، يعني أحاديث الجهر لم تثبت (فتح) كل ركعة أي أولها عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة يسمي في أول صلاته. بين السور: كالديباجة والطراز على أوائل السور، وقال مالك: ليست من القرآن إلا في النمل، فإنها بعض آية فيها. لیست من الفاتحة وقال الشافعي: هي من الفاتحة، وكذا من غيرها؛ لإجماعهم على كتابتها في المصاحف مع الأمر بتجريد المصاحف، وهي من أقوى الحجج، ولنا ما رواه ابن عباس لما أنه عليها كان لا يعرف فصل السور حتى ينزل عليه الله الرحمن الرحيم، رواه أبو داود، وأيضاً حديث قسمة الفاتحة، فإن فيه إذا قال العبد: . بسم =
And he recites the basmalah quietly: [i.e., the one not following (munfarid) says: 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' after the ta'awwudh]. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not recite it except in the first rak'ah, because it is not from al-Fatiha, it is only for opening, so it is specific to the first rak'ah like ta'awwudh. Al-Mu'alla narrated that he recites it in every rak'ah, and that is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); because although basmalah is definitively not made part of al-Fatiha, yet the khabar al-wahid necessitates acting upon it, so it becomes part of al-Fatiha practically. As for at the beginning of every surah, the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) do not recite it, and Muhammad says he recites it as a precaution. His statement: 'quietly' means absolutely, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to open the prayer with 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', and 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali used to recite it aloud. Our evidence: what is narrated from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) said: I prayed behind the Prophet, Abu Bakr, 'Umar, and 'Uthman, and I did not hear any of them recite 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' aloud. Abu Hurayra said that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not recite it aloud. What they narrated has no indication of reciting aloud, or it is interpreted that he recited aloud occasionally for teaching just as he occasionally recited aloud in Zuhr for teaching. As for what is narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and 'Uthman, Ibn Abd al-Barr said: the chains from them are not strong, meaning the hadiths of reciting aloud are not established. (Fath) Every rak'ah: i.e., at its beginning according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to Abu Hanifa he recites basmalah at the beginning of his prayer (only). Between surahs: like the preface and ornament at the beginnings of surahs. Malik said: It is not from the Quran except in al-Naml, where it is part of a verse. It is not from al-Fatiha. Al-Shafi'i said: It is from al-Fatiha and also from other surahs; due to the consensus on writing it in the musahaf with the command to keep the mushaf pure, and this is one of the strongest proofs. Our evidence: what Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not know the separation between surahs until 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' was revealed to him, narrated by Abu Dawud. Also the hadith of the division of al-Fatiha, for it says when the servant says: 'Bism...'
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about basmalah in prayer. The matn states that one recites basmalah quietly. The commentary explains intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: According to Abu Hanifa, basmalah is recited only in the first rak'ah because it is for opening, like ta'awwudh, and it is not part of al-Fatiha. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), it is recited in every rak'ah because they consider it part of al-Fatiha practically, based on a hadith that commands reciting it. At the beginning of each surah (when starting a new surah after Fatiha), the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) do not recite basmalah, but Muhammad recites it as ihtiyat. The Hanafi position is that basmalah is recited quietly (sirran), contrary to the Shafi'i school which recites it aloud. The proof for silence is the hadith of Anas that he did not hear the Prophet or the Caliphs recite it aloud. The Shafi'i evidence that the Prophet once recited aloud is dismissed as occasional for teaching. The passage also notes the disagreement about whether basmalah is part of al-Fatiha: Shafi'i says it is, Hanafi says it is not (though it is an independent Quranic verse used for separation). The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet did not know surah boundaries until basmalah was revealed.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiya): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited at the start of prayer or before reading Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (the view of Imam Muhammad), how is basmalah recited in prayer?
A) It is recited aloud in every rak'ah
B) It is recited silently only in the first rak'ah
C) It is recited silently in every rak'ah
D) It is not recited at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that basmalah is recited silently, as a separate verse for opening, and is not part of al-Fatiha; internal differences exist on the number of rak'ahs, but the relied-upon position is to recite it in every rak'ah.

Recitation of al-Fatiha and a Surah in Prayer
Explains the obligation of reciting al-Fatiha and a surah, and the evidence that basmalah is not a verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that reciting al-Fatiha and a surah is wajib in the Hanafi school, and explain the evidence that the basmalah is not a verse of al-Fatiha.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatiha and a surah is wajib; the basmalah is not part of al-Fatiha.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the obligatory recitations in prayer. You will learn the evidence from hadith and consensus that the basmalah is not a verse of al-Fatiha, and how this affects the obligation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: reciting al-Fatiha and a surah (or three verses). The text states this is wajib, not fard, because the proof is zanni al-thubut.
Wajib is a Hanafi legal category; omission makes the prayer valid but sinful.
2
Analyze the proof for basmalah not being a verse
Examine the hadith from Ali about Surah al-Mulk having 30 verses without basmalah, and the narration from A'ishah that Jibril recited 'Iqra' bismi rabbika' without basmalah. These demonstrate consensus that basmalah is not a verse of any surah.
The phrase 'Rabbi al-ʿālamīn, yaqūlu Allāhu: ḥamidanī ʿabdī' is also cited as proof that al-Fatiha begins with praise, not basmalah.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers basmalah a verse of al-Fatiha and recites it as part of the obligatory recitation. The Hanafi school differs based on the evidence presented.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have their proofs.
4
Determine the practical consequence
In the Hanafi school, one must recite basmalah separately before al-Fatiha, but it is not part of the wajib recitation. Omitting it does not invalidate the prayer, though it is recommended.
If al-Fatiha is omitted entirely, the prayer must be repeated (i'ada); omitting the surah does not require repetition.

وكبر بلا ،مد، وركع ووضع يديه على ركبتيه، وفرّج أصابعه وبسط ظهره وسوّى رأسه بعجزه، وسبّح فيه ثلاثاً ، ثم رفع رأسه،
بعد التسبيح ثلاثاً في الركوع

(طائي) سرا وعند الشافعي جهراً عند الجهر بالقراءة وعن مالك: لا يأتي الإمام بالتأمين، وهو رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة، والتشديد فيه خطأ فاحش تفسد به صلاته عند البعض، والفتوى على أنها لا تفسد وهو ليس . الفاتحة اتفاقاً، من ومعناه: استجب دعاءنا. (فتح) [رمز الحقائق: ٥٨/١] بلا مد [ أي بلا إشباع حركة الهمزة المفرط والمد الفاحش سواء كان في قوله: "الله"، أو في همزة "أكبر"؛ لأنه مبطل] حتى لو مد همزة الاسم أو الخبر فسدت، ولو في التحريمة لا يصير شارعاً، وخيف عليه الكفر إن قاصداً، ومد الباء خطأ كمد الهاء، أما مد لام الاسم فحسن ما لم يخرج عن حده. (فتح)
And not from every surah, and he recited al-Fatiha and a surah or three verses, and the imam and follower said Amin silently, meaning he recited with it a surah obligatorily. And he said the takbir without elongation, and bowed and placed his hands on his knees, and spread his fingers and straightened his back and made his head level with his hips, and glorified in it three times, then raised his head. (Tai) And 'surah' is accusative either as a conjunct or as a circumstantial accusative, and both are wajib, but al-Fatiha is more binding, such that one is commanded to repeat for leaving it but not for the surah. (Fath) Or three verses, and if the verse is long equivalent to three short verses, the prohibition of tahrim is removed, but the prohibition of tanzih is not removed except by the sunnah. (Fath) And the imam says Amin, i.e., he says 'Amin' with elongation and shortening and lightening. (Tai) Silently, and according to al-Shafi'i aloud when reciting aloud, and from Malik: the imam does not say Amin, and it is a narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifah, and emphasizing it is a gross error that corrupts his prayer according to some, and the fatwa is that it does not corrupt, and it is not from al-Fatiha by consensus, and its meaning: answer our supplication. (Fath) [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 58/1] Without elongation, i.e., without excessive stretching of the vowel of the hamzah and excessive elongation, whether in saying 'Allah' or in the hamzah of 'Akbar' because it invalidates. So if he elongates the hamzah of the name or the predicate, it becomes corrupt, and if in the tahrimah he does not become a beginner, and it is feared upon him disbelief if intentional, and elongating the ba' is an error like elongating the ha'. As for elongating the lam of the name, it is good as long as it does not exceed its limit. (Fath)
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a Hanafi fiqh text, is a ruling-with-proof section. It begins by stating the rulings on recitation in prayer: the worshipper must recite al-Fatiha and a surah (or three verses). This is wajib, not fard, according to the Hanafi school, which distinguishes between fard (obligatory with qat'i proof) and wajib (obligatory with zanni proof). The proof for not including the basmala as a verse of al-Fatiha is given: a hadith from Ali and a narration from A'ishah about the revelation of Surah al-Alaq without basmala. The text then discusses the ruling on Amin: the imam and follower say it silently. The Hanafi position is that it is said silently, contrary to the Shafi'i who say it aloud. A weak narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa held that the imam does not say Amin, but the relied-upon position is that he does, silently. The passage then discusses the takbir: elongation (madd) invalidates the prayer. The type of elongation that invalidates is specified: excessive stretching of the hamzah in 'Allah' or 'Akbar'. However, moderate elongation of the lam in 'Allah' is permissible. The authority weight of these rulings is Zahir al-Riwayah as the text is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a reliable matn.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): An obligation that is binding but established through zanni evidence, unlike fard which is from qat'i evidence.
تسمية (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' before recitation.
بسملة (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. The text argues it is not a verse of al-Fatiha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of omitting al-Fatiha during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the worshipper is commanded to repeat it.
C) The prayer is valid and no action is needed.
D) The prayer becomes makruh and must be corrected with sajdah sahw.

Key Takeaway
Reciting al-Fatiha and a surah is wajib in prayer; the basmalah is not a verse of al-Fatiha and is recited separately.

Saying Amin and Takbir Elongation in Prayer
Explains rulings on Amin and takbir elongation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Amin is said silently, and identify what elongation in the takbir invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Amin is said silently; excessive elongation in takbir invalidates prayer.

This lesson covers two practical rulings: the manner of saying Amin after al-Fatiha and the prohibition of elongation in the takbir. You will learn the evidence for saying Amin silently, the intra-madhhab difference, and the exact conditions under which elongation invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of saying Amin
The text states that the imam and follower say Amin silently. Determine the hukm: it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) according to the Hanafi school.
Some scholars consider it wajib, but the relied-upon position is sunnah.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that Abu Hanifa held the imam does not say Amin. However, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that both imam and follower say it silently.
This shows that even within a school, there can be variant narrations.
3
Compare with other schools
Al-Shafi'i holds Amin is said aloud when prayer is audible; Malik holds the imam does not say it. The Hanafi school takes the middle position: silently.
The practical difference is in the sound level of the congregation.
4
Understand the takbir elongation ruling
The text says 'bila madd' (without elongation). Excessive elongation of the hamzah in 'Allah' or 'Akbar' invalidates the prayer (fasid).
Moderate elongation of the lam in 'Allah' is permissible and even good.
5
Identify what constitutes invalidating elongation
Elongation in the hamzah of the name (Allah) or the predicate (Akbar) corrupts the prayer. If done intentionally in the takbir tahrimah, the prayer does not even begin.
The text warns of kufr if done intentionally with that intention.

Key Terms
آمين (amin): A word said after al-Fatiha meaning 'answer our supplication'.
مد (madd): Elongation of a vowel sound. In takbir, excessive madd invalidates.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'. Proper pronunciation is required; distortion invalidates.

Sunan of Ruku' and the Ruling on Tasbih
Details the sunan of ruku' and the dispute on tasbih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan of ruku' according to the Hanafi school and explain the dispute on the obligation of tasbih.

Core Idea
Spreading fingers, straightening back, and tasbih are sunnah muakkadah in ruku'.

Ruku' is a pillar of prayer, but within it there are specific recommended actions (sunan) that complete the bowing posture. This lesson covers the proper hand placement, back straightening, head level, and the much-debated ruling on tasbih – whether it is obligatory or highly recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan of ruku'
List the physical sunan: spreading fingers, grasping knees, straightening back, leveling head, and facing toes to qibla.
These apply specifically to men; women have different rules.
2
Understand the ruling on tasbih
The text states that saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal Azim' three times is sunnah; leaving it is makruh. Some Hanafi scholars consider it wajib, but the matn treats it as sunnah muakkadah.
The imam should not prolong excessively.
3
Note the madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i recommends extra supplications in ruku', while Imam Malik holds that no tasbih at all is required. The Hanafi position is the middle path.
All three positions are valid ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرج أصابعه أي أصابع يديه ليكون أمكن في أخذ الركبتين، فإن الأخذ والتفريج سنة . - ولا يندب التفريج إلا في هذه الحالة ولا الضم إلا في السجود - ولتقع رؤوس الأصابع متوجهة إلى القبلة، وفيما وراء ذلك تترك على العادة. وتفريج الأصابع سنة الركوع للرجال لا للنساء، وينبغي أن يزاد محافياً عضديه . ملصقاً . كعبيه مستقبلاً أصابعه، فإنها سنة (فتح) وبسط ظهره حتى لو وضع على ظهره قدح ماء لاستقر. (طائي) بعجزه: وهو نصفه المؤخر، أراد أن لا يرفع رأسه إلى فوق ولا ينكسه إلى أسفل. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٨/١] ثلاثاً: أي مطلقاً، وترك الثلاث مكروه، وكلما زاد فهو أفضل للمنفرد بعد أن يكون الختم على وتر، وأما الإمام فلا يزيد على وجه يمل القوم، وعن الشافعي أنه يزيد فيه: "اللهم لك ركعت ولك خشعت، ولك أسلمت، وعليك توكلت"، وفي السجود: "سجد وجهي للذي خلقه وصوّره، وشق سمعه وبصره، فتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين"، وعن مالك: أنه لا تسبيح في الركوع. (فتح، عيني)  كتاب الصلاة ٨٥ فصل في كيفية الصلاة واكتفى الإمام بالتسميع، والمؤتم بالتحميد والمنفرد بهما، ثم كبر، ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه بعكس النهوض، وسجد بأنفه وجبهته، وكره بأحدهما على الأرض بالتسميع: أي التسميع فقط؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا قال الإمام: سمع الله لمن حمده، فقولوا: ربنا ولك الحمد" قسم بينهما، وهي تنافي الشركة، فلا يقول الإمام ربنا ولك الحمد وقالا : يقوله الإمام سراً؛ لأنه عليه كان يجمع بينهما؛ ولأنه حرض غيره فلا ينسى نفسه، وقال الشافعي: يأتي الإمام والمأموم بالذكرين؛ لأن المؤتم يتابع الإمام فيما يفعل. وسمع بمعنى قبل، يقال: سمع الأمير كلام فلان أي قبله وهو دعاء لقبول الحمد، واللام في "لمن" للمنفعة، والهاء في "حمده" للسكنة والاستراحة، وقيل: هاء الضمير. (فتح) بالتحميد: أي يكتفي المؤتم بالتحميد فقط. وصيغ التحميد أربع ربنا لك الحمد، وربنا ولك الحمد، واللهم ربنا لك الحمد، واللهم ربنا ولك الحمد، وكل من . هذه الأربع منقول عنه عليه، لكن "اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد" أحسن وأفضل، وقيل: اللهم ربنا لك الحمد" بدون الواو، واختلفوا في الواو، فقيل زائدة، وقيل: عاطفة، تقديره: ربنا حمدناك ولك الحمد، وقال الشافعي: يأتي المؤتم بالتسميع أيضاً. والمنفرد بهما: أي يأتي المنفرد بالتسبيح والتحميد، وهو الأصح. (طائي)
And he spread his fingers, i.e., the fingers of his hands, to be better able to grasp the knees, for grasping and spreading are sunnah. And spreading is not recommended except in this case, nor joining except in prostration. And so that the tips of the fingers face the qibla, and beyond that they are left as customary. Spreading the fingers is a sunnah of ruku' for men, not women. And it is recommended to add: making his upper arms close, his heels together, facing his toes, for that is sunnah. (Fath) And he straightened his back so that if a cup of water were placed on his back, it would stay. (Tai) 'With his hips': i.e., the back half, meaning he should neither raise his head upwards nor lower it downwards. [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 58/1] 'Three times': i.e., absolutely, and leaving the three is makruh. And every increase is better for the individual as long as it ends on an odd number. As for the imam, he should not increase in a way that bores the people. And from al-Shafi'i that he adds: 'O Allah, to You I have bowed, to You I have humbled, to You I have submitted, and in You I have trusted' and in prostration: 'My face has prostrated to the One who created it and fashioned it, and opened its hearing and sight, so blessed is Allah, the Best of creators.' And from Malik that there is no tasbih in ruku'. (Fath, Ayni) [PAGE_086] Book of Prayer 85 Chapter on the Manner of Prayer And the imam suffices with tasmi', and the follower with tahmid, and the individual with both. Then he said takbir, and placed his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, opposite to rising, and prostrated with his nose and forehead, and he disliked with one of them on the ground. 'With tasmi'': i.e., only tasmi'; due to his statement: 'When the imam says: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say: Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' – he divided between them, and it precludes partnership, so the imam does not say 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd'. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The imam says it silently, because he used to combine both, and because he urges others so he should not forget himself. And al-Shafi'i said: The imam and follower say both remembrances, because the follower follows the imam in what he does. 'Sami'a' meaning accepted; it is said: The amir heard (i.e., accepted) the speech of so-and-so. It is a supplication for acceptance of praise. The 'lam' in 'liman' is for benefit, and the 'ha' in 'hamidah' is for rest and repose, and it is said: it is the pronoun. (Fath) 'With tahmid': i.e., the follower suffices with the tahmid alone. The forms of tahmid are four: 'Rabbana laka al-hamd', 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd', 'Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd', 'Allahumma Rabbana wa laka al-hamd', and all of these are transmitted from him, but 'Allahumma Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' is best and most excellent. And it is said: 'Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd' without the waw. They differed over the waw: some said it is redundant, others said it is conjunctive, its estimation: 'Rabbana we have praised You and to You is all praise.' And al-Shafi'i said: the follower also says the tasmi'. 'And the individual with both': i.e., the individual says both tasbi and tahmid, and that is the most correct. (Tai)
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is an inter-madhhab dispute. It first details the sunan of ruku': spreading fingers, straightening the back, leveling the head, and saying tasbih at least three times. The imam should not prolong. It mentions that al-Shafi'i adds extra supplications in ruku' and sujud, while Malik holds that tasbih is not required. The main dispute concerns the remembrances when rising from ruku'. The Hanafi position is that the imam says only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (tasmi'), the follower says only 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' (tahmid), and the individual says both. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet divided the statements. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the imam should also say the tahmid silently. Al-Shafi'i holds that both imam and follower say both. The text also discusses the different forms of tahmid, preferring the one with 'Allahumma' and 'wa'. The authority weight: the primary ruling is from the hadith, with the Hanafi position being the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
تسبيح (tasbih): Glorifications said in ruku' and sujud, e.g., 'Subhana Rabbiyal Azim'.
تفريج الأصابع (tafriq al-asabi'): Spreading the fingers while grasping the knees during ruku'.
بسط الظهر (bast al-dhahr): Straightening the back so it is level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal Azim' three times in ruku'?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah muakkadah.
C) It is mustahab.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of ruku' are highly recommended, and tasbih is sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school.

The Division of Tasmi' and Tahmid Between Imam and Follower
Explains the dispute on tasmi' and tahmid based on a hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tasmi' and tahmid, explain the dalil from the hadith, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The imam says only tasmi', the follower only tahmid, the individual says both.

When rising from ruku', specific remembrances are said. A famous hadith divides the statements between the imam and the follower. The Hanafi school adheres to this division strictly, while the Shafi'i school has both say everything. This lesson examines the proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The imam says only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (tasmi'), the follower says only 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' (tahmid), and the individual says both.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the imam should also say tahmid silently.
2
Analyze the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say Rabbana wa laka al-hamd.' The division (qasm) between the two statements negates partnership (shirkah).
The term 'qasm' here means equal division, not just separation.
3
Examine the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the follower should follow the imam in all actions, so the follower should also say tasmi'. The Hanafis respond that this hadith specifically divides the roles, overriding the general principle.
The practical result: in Hanafi mosques, only the imam says tasmi' aloud; in Shafi'i mosques, both do.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is how the congregational prayer sounds. The Hanafi way preserves the hadith's literal division; the Shafi'i way emphasizes following the imam.
Both are valid; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
