Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Sunnah Recitation and Lengthening in Prayer
Defines the sunnah recitation and lengthening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the sunnah recitation in travel and residence, classify the surahs of al-Mufassal, and explain the ruling on lengthening the first rak'ah.

Core Idea
Sunnah recitation varies by prayer and context: travel allows any surah; residence prescribes specific sections of al-Mufassal; lengthening the first rak'ah is sunnah.

Beyond the obligatory one verse, the Hanafi school encourages a fuller recitation as sunnah. The sunnah includes reciting al-Fatihah plus another surah, with specific recommendations for each prayer. This lesson will clarify the sunnah rules, the categorization of al-Mufassal, and the preferred lengthening of the first rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Travel and Residence Rulings
In travel, the sunnah is to recite al-Fatihah and any surah one wishes, due to ease. In residence, specific surahs are recommended based on the prayer time.
Travel here means a journey of three days' distance or more (or the custom of the locale).
2
Identify the Sections of al-Mufassal
Al-Mufassal is the last seventh of the Quran, from Surah Muhammad (or al-Fath) to the end. It is divided into three parts: long (tiwal), medium (awsat), and short (qisar). These correspond to different prayers.
Long surahs are from al-Hujurat to al-Buruj; medium from al-Buruj to Lam Yakun; short from Lam Yakun to the end.
3
Apply the Sunnah to Each Prayer
For Fajr and Zuhr: recite a long surah from al-Mufassal (e.g., al-Buruj). For Asr and Isha: a medium surah. For Maghrib: a short surah.
This is the recommended practice; reciting any surah is permissible.
4
Understand the Ruling on Lengthening the First Rak'ah
It is sunnah to make the first rak'ah longer than the second, by about two-thirds of the recitation in the first and one-third in the second. This applies to all prayers according to the mufta bihi.
The preference is for a clear difference, but even a large disparity is not sinful.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Lengthening
Imam Muhammad and the mufta bihi say lengthening is sunnah in all prayers. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in another view say no lengthening, except possibly in Fajr. Lengthening the second over the first is only allowed in Fajr.
The fatwa is on lengthening the first in all prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية الصلاة
وفرض القراءة آية، وسنتها في السفر الفاتحة وأيُّ سورة شاء، وفي الحضر طوالُ المفصل لو فجراً أو ظهراً، وأوساطه لو عصراً أو عشاء، وقصاره لو مغرباً، وتطال أولى

وفرض القراءة: مطلقاً ولو قصيرة من الفاتحة أو غيرها آية الآية لغة: العلامة، وعرفاً طائفة من القرآن، وأطلقها من فعم القصيرة، وهو قول أبي حنيفة؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ﴾ (المزمل: ٢٠) إلا أن ما دون الآية خارج، وقالا ثلاث آيات قصار؛ لأن القارئ بما دونها لا قارئاً عرفاً، سواء كانت يسمى من الفاتحة أو غيرها أو آية طويلة، وقال الشافعي: قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعة فرض، وقال مالك: الفاتحة وضم سورة فرض، وهذا إذا قرأ آية قصيرة هي ثلاث كلمات، نحو: ﴿فَقُتِلَ كَيْفَ قَدَّرَ﴾ (المدثر : ١٩) أو كلمتان نحو: ﴿ثُمَّ نَظَرَ﴾ (المدثر: ۲۱)، ولو قرأ آية أي كلمة واحدة كـ ﴿مُدْهَامَّتَانِ﴾ (الرحمن: ٦٤) أو حرف باعتبار صورة الكتابة كـ ﴿ص﴾ و ﴿ن﴾ و ﴿ق﴾، فإنها آيات عند بعض القراء، فالأصح أنه لا يجوز، ولو قرأ آية طويلة في ركعتين كآية الكرسي والمداينة، الأصح أنه يجوز عنده.

وسنتها في السفر بعد الفاتحة أي سورة شاء لكان أولى؛ لإيهامه أن قراءة الفاتحة سنة، أقول : الإيهام باق؛ فإنه على ما ذكره يوهم أن قراءة أي سورة شاء سنة مع أنها واجبة، ويمكن أن يجاب بأن المحكوم عليه بالسنية المجموع لا الجميع.

وأي سورة شاء لأن مبنى السفر على التخفيف إذا كان على عجلة من السير وإلا فيقرأ في الفجر والظهر نحو البروج، وفي العصر والعشاء دون ذلك، وفي المغرب بالقصار جداً.

طوال المفصل: ظاهره الاستغراق، والمراد قراءة اثنتين تامتين من السور الطويلة من هذا القسم مع الفاتحة، والطوال بكسر الطاء جمع طويل، والمفصل وهو السبع السابع من القرآن سمي به لكثرة فصوله، وهو من سورة "محمد"، وقيل: من "الفتح"، إلى آخر القرآن والطوال منه أو من "الحجرات" إلى آخر "البروج".

أوساطه: أي أوساط المفصل، وهي من "البروج" إلى "لم يكن".

وقصاره: أي قصار المفصل، وهي من "لم يكن" إلى آخر القرآن.

وتطال: أي إطالة القراءة في الركعة الأولى على الثانية مسنون إجماعاً، وفي سائر الصلوات كذلك عند محمد، وفي "المعراج" وعليه الفتوى وقوله أحب وعندهما لا تطال، ثم يعتبر التطويل من حيث الآي إذا كان بين ما يقرأ في الأولى وبين ما يقرأ في الثانية تفاوت من حيث الآي، أما إذا كان بين الآي تفاوت طولاً وقصراً فيعتبر التفاوت من حيث الكلمات والحروف، وينبغي أن يكون التفاوت بقدر الثلث والثلثين، الثلثان في الأولى والثلث في الثانية، وهذا بيان الاستحباب. أما بيان الحكم فالتفاوت وإن كان فاحشا لا بأس به، وإطالة الثانية على الفجر فقط.
Chapter on the manner of prayer. The obligatory [recitation] is a verse, and its sunnah in travel is al-Fatihah and whatever surah one wishes, and in residence the long ones of al-Mufassal for Fajr or Zuhr, and its medium ones for Asr or Isha, and its short ones for Maghrib, and lengthening [the first rak'ah] is preferable. The obligatory recitation: absolutely, even if a short verse from al-Fatihah or other, is a verse. 'Ayah' linguistically means a sign, and technically a portion of the Quran. And [Abu Hanifa] considers even a short one, which is the saying of Abu Hanifa, due to the generality of His statement 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20) except that less than a verse is excluded. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said three short verses, because the reciter of less than that is not called a reciter customarily, whether from al-Fatihah or other or a long verse. I say: the implication remains, for according to what he mentioned it implies that reciting any surah one wishes is sunnah while it is obligatory, and it can be answered that what is ruled as sunnah is the sum, not the individual. Key Terms
المفصل (al-Mufassal): The seventh seventh (or last part) of the Quran, from Surah Muhammad (or al-Fath) to the end, named for its many divisions (fusuul).
تطال (tataal): Lengthening of the first rak'ah's recitation over the second.

Prohibition of Specifying a Surah (Ta'yin) in Prayer
Ruling on designating a surah for a specific prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying a particular surah for a specific prayer and identify when it becomes makruh.

Core Idea
Persistently specifying a surah for a prayer, other than al-Fatihah, is makruh because it implies preference.

The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the issue of ta'yin — designating a specific surah to be recited in a specific prayer. While al-Fatihah is wajib in every rak'ah, the Hanafi school holds that no other surah is prescribed for any particular prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling: why persistent specification is disliked, the exceptions for sunnah practices, and the nuance between occasional and habitual recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text begins 'لم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصلاة' – nothing is specified. This is the foundational ruling: ta'yin is not prescribed.
2
Determine the hukm level
The text says 'يكره التعيين' – it is disliked. The passage explains that the dislike is tied to persistence (المداومة).
The dislike is tanzihi (makruh tanzih).
3
Differentiate between al-Fatihah and others
Al-Fatihah is wajib; its specification is obligatory. The dispute with Shafi'i is whether it is fard or wajib, not on the obligation itself.
The issue is the basis of obligation, not the obligation itself.
4
Examine the exception
The Prophet's sunnah of reciting specific surahs on certain occasions (e.g., al-A'la and al-Ghashiyah for Jumu'ah) is not disliked; rather, it is recommended to occasionally recite them.
What is sunnah is exempt from the dislike.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a person consistently recites Surah al-Ikhlas in the first rak'ah of Fajr out of habit and believes it is necessary, it is makruh. But if they vary or do it occasionally, it is permissible.
The key is persistence (الملازمة).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصلاة، ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت،

وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب أو صلى على النبي عليه، والنائي كالقريب.

في افتراض الإنصات

• الأولى تكره إجماعاً، أي تنزيها في غير ما وردت به السنة كما أخرجه الشيخان من أنه لي: كان يقرأ في أولى الجمعة والعيدين بـ"الأعلى" وفي الثانية بـ"الغاشية"، وهي أطول من الأولى بأكثر من ثلاث، ويكره التفاوت بثلاث آيات وأما بآية أو آيتين فلا يكره.

لصلاة: [على سبيل الفرض، بل تعيين الفاتحة على وجه الوجوب، ويكره التعيين.]

مطلقاً سواء كان فجر الجمعة أو لا، يعني كره تعيين سورة لبعض من الصلوات أو لكلها يريد سوى الفاتحة، وأشار إلى أنه لا خلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي في تعيين الفاتحة، إنما الخلاف في جهة التعيين، فعنده للفرضية، وعندنا للوجوب، وقال الشافعي: أن يتخذ سورة السجدة" وسورة "الدهر" بفجر يوم الجمعة، وكراهة التعيين إذا عين ولازم عليها، فإن كان يقرأها أحياناً فلا بأس به، وقيل: الملازمة إنما تكره إذا لم يعتقد الجواز بغيره، أما إذا اعتقد الجواز بغيره وإنما قرأها؛ لأنها أيسر عليه فلا يكره، والحق أن المداومة مطلقاً مكروهة سواء رأه حتماً أو لا؛ إذ دليل الكراهة وهو إيهام التفضيل موجود، ومقتضى الدليل عدم المداومة لا المداومة، بل يستحب قراءة ذلك أحياناً، وكذا قالوا: السنة أن يقرأ في ركعتي الفجر بـ"الكافرون" و"الإخلاص".

يقرأ المؤتم: ولو الفاتحة في السرية فإن قرأ كره تحريماً. بل يستمع وينصت لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنْصِتُوا﴾ (الأعراف:٢٠٤) وأكثر أهل التفسير على أن هذه خطاب للمقتديين، وقال مالك: يقرأ في السرية لا في الجهرية، وقال الشافعي: يقرأ الفاتحة في الكل؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب"، ولنا الآية المتقدمة وحديث أبي هريرة: "فإذا قرأ الإمام فأنصتوا" فما في "الهداية": ويستحسن قراءة الفاتحة في السرية احتياطاً فيما يروى عن محمد ضعيف، والمشهور من مذهب أئمتنا ومشايخنا أنه مكروه كراهة تحريم؛ لما جاء فيه من التشدد عن الصحابة على ما أخرجه محمد في الموطأ والطحاوي في شرح معاني الآثار، ثم وجوب الاستماع لا يخص المقتدي ولا كون القارئ إماماً؛ لأن العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب، والإمام مأمور بإنصاته عما سوى القرآن حين قراءته، والمقتدي مأمور باستماع القرآن وإنصاته سواء كانت الصلاة سرية أو جهرية، وقال في المستخلص: قال الشافعي: يقرأ الفاتحة؛ لأن الفاتحة ركن من الأركان، فيشتركان أي الإمام والمأموم فيه ولنا قوله عليه السلام: "من كان له إمام فقراءة الإمام قراءة له، وعليه إجماع الصحابة، وقال علي: "من قرأ خلف الإمام فقد أخطأ الفطرة، وعن سعد بن أبي وقاص وزيد بن ثابت: "من قرأ خلف الإمام فلا صلاة له".

وإن قرأ إلخ أي يستمع المؤتم ولو قرأ الإمام آية الترغيب في ثواب الله أو الترهيب من عقابه لا يسأل الجنة ولا يتعوذ من النار.

أو صلى: في الخطبة إلا أن يقرأ الخطيب: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمُوا﴾ (الأحزاب:٥٦) فيصلي السامع في نفسه.

والنائي: أي البعيد الذي لا يسمع الخطبة.
And nothing specific from the Quran is designated for a prayer, and the follower does not recite but listens and remains silent.

And if [the imam] recites a verse of encouragement or deterrence or delivers a sermon or sends blessings upon the Prophet, [the follower does not respond], and the distant one is like the near one.

Regarding the obligation of silence.

• The first is disliked by consensus, i.e., tanzihan, except what the sunnah has indicated, as the two Shaykhs narrated that he (ﷺ) used to recite in the first of Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids "al-A'la" and in the second "al-Ghashiyah", which is longer than the first by more than three [verses]. And a difference of three verses is disliked, but of one or two verses it is not disliked.

For a prayer: [on the basis of fard, rather the designation of al-Fatihah is wajib, and designation [of other surahs] is disliked.]

Absolutely, whether it is Fajr of Jumu'ah or not, meaning the designation of a surah for some prayers or all is disliked – he intends other than al-Fatihah. And he indicated that there is no disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i on designating al-Fatihah; the disagreement is only on the basis of designation: with him for fard, with us for wujub. And al-Shafi'i said: that one takes Surah al-Sajdah and Surah al-Dahr for Fajr of Jumu'ah. And the dislike of designation is when one specifies and persists on it; if one recites it occasionally, there is no harm. And it is said: persistence is only disliked if one does not consider permissibility with other than it; but if one considers permissibility with other and recites it because it is easier, then it is not disliked. The truth is that continuous practice is disliked absolutely, whether one considers it binding or not, because the reason for dislike – which is implying preference – exists, and the requirement of the evidence is non-continuity, not continuity. Rather, it is recommended to recite that occasionally. And likewise they said: the sunnah is to recite in the two rak'ahs of Fajr "al-Kafirun" and "al-Ikhlas".

The follower recites: even al-Fatihah in silent [prayers] – if he recites, it is tahriman makruh. Rather, he listens and remains silent due to His statement 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' (7:204), and most commentators hold that this is addressed to the followers. And Malik said: he recites in silent prayers, not in loud ones. And al-Shafi'i said: he recites al-Fatihah in all [prayers], due to his (ﷺ) statement: 'No prayer except with the Fatihah of the Book.' And our proof is the aforementioned verse and the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'When the imam recites, be silent.' So what is in al-Hidayah: 'It is deemed commendable to recite al-Fatihah in silent prayers as a precaution' – transmitted from Muhammad is weak, and the well-known view of our imams and scholars is that it is tahriman makruh, due to the strictness that came from the Companions as Muhammad narrated in al-Muwatta' and al-Tahawi in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar. Then the obligation of listening is not specific to the follower nor to the imam being the reciter, because consideration is to the generality of the wording, not to the specific occasion. The imam is commanded to be silent from other than the Quran while reciting, and the follower is commanded to listen to the Quran and be silent whether the prayer is silent or loud. And it is said in al-Mustakhlas: al-Shafi'i said: he recites al-Fatihah because al-Fatihah is a pillar of the pillars, so the imam and the follower share in it. And our proof is his (ﷺ) statement: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is his recitation,' and upon this is the consensus of the Companions. And 'Ali said: 'Whoever recites behind the imam has deviated from the natural disposition.' And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Zayd ibn Thabit: 'Whoever recites behind the imam, there is no prayer for him.'

And if [the imam] recites, etc., i.e., the follower listens, even if the imam recites a verse of encouragement about Allah's reward or deterrence from His punishment, he does not ask for Paradise nor seek refuge from hellfire.

Or he prays: in the sermon, except that the preacher recites 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him and greet him' (33:56) – then the listener prays in himself.

And al-Na'i: i.e., the distant one who does not hear the sermon.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two interconnected rulings: (1) no specific surah is designated for any prayer, and (2) the follower (mu'tamm) must listen and remain silent, not recite. The text begins by stating that nothing specific from the Quran is prescribed for a particular prayer – it is disliked to always recite a specific surah in a specific prayer (except al-Fatihah, which is wajib). The commentary clarifies that the dislike is tahrimi when there is persistent adherence, as it implies superiority of that surah. However, if one recites it occasionally or because it is easier, it is not disliked. Even the practice of reciting specific surahs like al-Sajdah and al-Dahr in Fajr of Jumu'ah is disliked if done consistently. The sunnah is to vary and occasionally recite them. Then the ruling for the follower: he must not recite even al-Fatihah; rather, he listens and remains silent. This is supported by the Quranic verse (7:204) and Hadith (Abu Hurayrah: 'When the imam recites, be silent'). The majority of commentators interpret the verse for followers. The passage contrasts this with Shafi'i's view that the follower must recite al-Fatihah in all prayers, and Malik's view that he recites in silent prayers but not loud ones. The Hanafi position is that reciting behind the imam is tahriman makruh, based on strong evidence: the verse, the hadith, and statements of Companions (Ali, Sa'd, Zayd). The imam's recitation suffices for the follower. The passage also notes that the obligation to listen is general, not limited to the follower, and the imam also must be silent from other speech. Even if the imam recites a verse of encouragement or threat, the follower does not respond (no asking for Paradise or seeking refuge). Similarly, during the sermon, if the preacher recites a verse, the listener may send blessings upon the Prophet but only in his heart. The distant one (al-na'i) who cannot hear the sermon is like the near one in rulings.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower in prayer who prays behind an imam.
الإنصات (al-insat): Silence and attentive listening, specifically during Quran recitation in prayer or sermon.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying a particular surah to be recited consistently in a specific prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on someone who persistently recites a specific surah (e.g., al-Ikhlas) in a specific prayer out of habit, without considering it necessary?
A) Makruh tahriman
B) Makruh tanzih
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Persistent specification of any surah other than al-Fatihah for a specific prayer is makruh tanzih; occasional recitation is permissible.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam
Ruling on follower's recitation and the obligation of silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation behind the imam, explain the evidence, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In congregational prayer, the follower must not recite; the imam's recitation suffices.

One of the most well-known differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is whether the follower (mu'tamm) recites al-Fatihah behind the imam. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the Hanafi position clearly: the follower listens and remains silent, and recitation behind the imam is tahriman makruh. This lesson examines the textual evidence from the Quran and Hadith, the opposing view, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
The text says 'ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت' and later 'يقرأ المؤتم: ولو الفاتحة في السرية فإن قرأ كره تحريماً'. The follower must not recite; if they do, it is makruh tahriman.
This applies to both loud and silent prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quran verse 7:204 is cited: 'وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنْصِتُوا'. The verse commands listening and silence. Most commentators interpret it during prayer.
Also used: hadith of Abu Hurayrah 'When the imam recites, be silent'.
3
Examine the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'No prayer except with Fatihah of the Book' to require al-Fatihah for everyone, including the follower.
Shafi'i considers al-Fatihah a rukn that cannot be dropped.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The verse and hadith of Abu Hurayrah take precedence. The hadith 'من كان له إمام فقراءة الإمام له قراءة' attributes the imam's recitation to the follower. Also consensus of Companions is cited.
The absolute command 'no prayer except with Fatihah' is restricted to one praying alone.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
In Hanafi mosques, followers do not recite; in Shafi'i ones, they must recite al-Fatihah. This affects how one prays when visiting a different madhhab mosque.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصلاة، ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت،

وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب أو صلى على النبي عليه، والنائي كالقريب.

في افتراض الإنصات

• الأولى تكره إجماعاً، أي تنزيها في غير ما وردت به السنة كما أخرجه الشيخان من أنه لي: كان يقرأ في أولى الجمعة والعيدين بـ"الأعلى" وفي الثانية بـ"الغاشية"، وهي أطول من الأولى بأكثر من ثلاث، ويكره التفاوت بثلاث آيات وأما بآية أو آيتين فلا يكره.

لصلاة: [على سبيل الفرض، بل تعيين الفاتحة على وجه الوجوب، ويكره التعيين.]

According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for the follower's obligation to listen and be silent?
A) Hadith only
B) Quran verse 7:204 and hadith
C) Consensus only
D) Qiyas

Key Takeaway
The follower in congregational prayer must listen and remain silent; recitation is makruh tahriman.

Ruling on Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Establishes the ruling of congregational prayer and refutes claims of it being obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer and explain why it is not fard, using the hadith evidence about increased reward.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah; praying alone is valid but less rewarded.

This lesson examines the legal ruling of congregational prayer (ṣalāt al-jamāʿah) in the Hanafi school. While some scholars deem it obligatory, the Hanafi position—supported by the Prophet’s hadith—classifies it as a strongly recommended act (sunnah mu’akkadah). You will learn the evidence and reasoning that underpin this ruling, and why missing congregation does not incur sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify that the act under discussion is congregational prayer for the five daily prayers, Tarawih, and Witr. The author states it is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
This is the core Hanafi position.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof cited is the hadith: 'The prayer of a man in congregation is superior to his prayer in his house or market by twenty-some degrees.'
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'exceeds' (tazīdu) indicates superiority (tafdīl), not obligation (ījāb). The hadith implies that solitary prayer is permissible and valid, albeit with less reward. If congregation were fard 'ayn, solitary prayer would be invalid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text mentions that some scholars (Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Zahiris) consider congregation fard 'ayn. Others said fard kifayah. The Hanafis hold it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The ikhtilaf centers on whether the evidence conveys obligation or recommendation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi response uses the same hadith: if congregation were fard kifayah, the Prophet would not have threatened to burn houses of those who missed it, and if it were fard 'ayn, solitary prayer would be impermissible. Hence, it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
This is the argument from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنة مؤكدة في الصلوات الخمس وما في حكمها كالتراويح والوتر بعدها دون النفل. (ط)] أي في الفرائض شبهة بالواجب حتى استدل بملازمتها على وجود الإيمان وقيل فريضة وقيل فرض كفاية، وقيل: فرض عين، وبه قال أحمد وأهل الظاهر، ومن فاتته جماعة لا يجب عليه الطلب في مسجد آخر، وتسقط بالأعذار كالمرض والإقعاد والزمانة والعمي والفلاجة والمطر والبرد والظلمة الشديدة رمز الحقائق ٦٥/١٢] ونحو ذلك، والحجة على القائلين بفرضيتها قوله عليه: "صلاة الرجل في جماعة تزيد على صلاته في بيته، وصلاته في سوقه بضعاً وعشرين درجة"، وهذا يفيد جواز الصلاة انفراداً، فلو كانت الجماعة فرض عين لما جاز صلاته منفرداً، ولو كانت فرض كفاية لكانت تسقط عمن لم يحضر الجماعة بفعله عليا وفعل أصحابه، ولما هم بإحراق بيوتهم. (عيني، فتح)
[Congregational prayer] is a strongly confirmed sunnah in the five prayers and their equivalents, like Tarawih and Witr after them, but not supererogatory. (Tahawi) That is, in the obligatory prayers, it is similar to wajib, to the extent that adherence to it is used as evidence of the existence of faith. And it was said [it is] fard, and it was said fard kifayah, and it was said fard 'ayn, and Ahmad and the Zahiris said that. The one who misses congregation is not required to seek it in another mosque, and it is dropped due to excuses like illness, chronic illness, disability, blindness, paralysis, rain, cold, intense darkness (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 65/12) and the like. The argument against those who say it is obligatory is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The prayer of a man in congregation is twenty-some degrees better than his prayer in his house and his prayer in the market.' This indicates the permissibility of praying alone. For if congregation were fard 'ayn, it would not be permissible to pray alone. And if it were fard kifayah, it would have been dropped from those who did not attend congregation by the action of Ali and his Companions, and he would not have intended to burn their houses. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling (ḥukm) of congregational prayer (jamā'ah). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, asserts in the matn that it is a 'sunnah mu'akkadah' (strongly confirmed sunnah) for the five daily prayers, as well as Tarawih and Witr after them, but not for sunnah prayers. The commentary (from Tahawi, 'Ayni, and Fath al-Qadir) explains that it occupies a position similar to wajib in the obligatory prayers; indeed, adherence to it is used as evidence of one's faith. Several opinions exist: some said it is fard, others fard kifayah, others fard 'ayn (the last being the view of Imam Ahmad and the Zahiris). The author refutes these by citing the hadith: 'The prayer of a man in congregation exceeds his prayer alone by twenty-some degrees.' This hadith implies that praying alone is permissible because it is still valid but inferior; if it were fard 'ayn, it would not be permissible at all. If it were fard kifayah, the obligation would have been discharged by Ali and the Companions' action, and the Prophet would not have intended to burn the houses of those who missed it. Thus, the correct position is that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not an obligation. It is also not required to seek another mosque if one misses congregation, and the obligation is dropped for valid excuses.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A strongly recommended act; omission is disliked (makruh tanzihan) but not sinful.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if some perform it, the rest are absolved.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation; every accountable person must perform it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is a strongly confirmed sunnah; while its reward is vastly multiplied, praying alone is permissible and valid.

The Most Deserving Imam: A‘lam vs Aqra’
Establishes imamate hierarchy with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for imamate and explain why the most knowledgeable (a‘lam) is preferred over the best reciter (aqra’), including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Knowledge of prayer rulings matters more than mere recitation quality.

Choosing an imam is not arbitrary; the Shari‘ah provides a clear priority order. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa’iq lays out that the most knowledgeable in fiqh al-salah comes first, then the best reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest. But not all Hanafi imams agreed on the first two – Abu Yusuf placed recitation first. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy
Read the matn: a‘lam → aqra’ → awra‘ → asann. Note that the commentary clarifies that a‘lam means knowledge of what corrects and invalidates prayer.
The matn is the core rule; the sharh expands and defends it.
2
Spot the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf disagreed, arguing aqra’ should come first based on the hadith 'yā’ummul qawma aqra’uhum'. Identify his position and his proof.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school – not a rejection of the madhhab.
3
Analyse the rebuttal
The authors (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond with the hadith of Abu Bakr and the principle that the best reciter among the Sahaba was also the most knowledgeable. Understand how they harmonise the texts.
The key is that the hadith on reciter is interpreted in light of how the Sahaba studied the Qur'an – with its meanings.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's: a‘lam first. Confirm why this is the case (tarjih).
The commentators (Fath al-Qadir) support this with the incident of Abu Bakr.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given two potential imams: one knows the rulings of prayer well but recites slowly; the other recites beautifully but does not know what invalidates prayer. Apply the hierarchy.
The knowledgeable one is preferred, even if his recitation is weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأعلم [ أي بأحكام الصلاة إذا كان يحفظ فرض القراءة. (فتح)] أي الأعلم بما يصلح الصلاة ويفسدها إذا علم من القراءة قدر ما تقوم به سنة القراءة، وقال أبو يوسف: الأقرأ أحق عملاً بظاهر ما في الصحيح: "يؤم القوم أقرؤهم لكتاب الله تعالى، فإن كانوا في القراءة سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة، فإن كانوا في السنة سواء فأقدمهم هجرة، فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً"، ولهما قوله عليه: "مروا أبا بكر فليصل بالناس"، وكان ثمه من هو أقرأ منه بدليل ما روي أقرؤكم أبي، فلم يبق إلا لكونه أعلم، وقدم الأقرأ في الحديث؛ لأنهم كانوا يتلقون القرآن بأحكامه حتى روي عن عمر اهل الله أنه حفظ البقرة في اثنتي عشرة سنة، وقال ابن عمر ه: "ما كانت تنزل سورة إلا ونعلم أمرها ونهيها وزجرها وحلالها وحرامها. فيلزم من كونه أقرأ أن يكون أعلم. تتمة: حفظ القرآن من الصحابة أبي بن كعب وزيد بن ثابت ومعاذ بن جبل، وأبو زيد الأنصاري، وعثمان بن عفان واختلف في أبي الدرداء، وعبادة، وتميم الداري (فتح)
ثم الأورع ثم الأسن، وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة . لنفره الناس عنه
ثم الأورع: أي المحترز عن شبهة الحرام؛ لقوله عليه: "إن سركم أن يتقبل الله صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم، فإنهم وفدكم أي رسلكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم"؛ ولأنه عليها قدم أقدمهم هجرة ولا هجرة اليوم، فأقمنا الأورع مقامها، وعلى تقديم الأورع على الأسن جرى الأكثر عكس ما في "المحيط". (فتح) الأسن: لقوله لمالك بن حويرث ولصاحب له : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا ثم أقيما وليؤمكما أكبر كما"؛ ولأن في تقديم الأسن تكثير الجماعة، فإن كانوا في السن سواء فأحسنهم وجهاً أو أحسنهم خلقا ومعاشرة، فإن كانوا سواء فأشرفهم نسبا، فإن تساووا يقرع بينهم، ولو قدموا غير الأولى أساءوا بلا إثم، ولو أم قوماً وهم له كارهون لفساد فيه، أو لأن غيره هناك أحق بالإمامة منه كره له ذلك تحريماً؛ لحديث أبي داود: "لا يقبل الله صلاة من تقدم قوماً وهم له كارهون، والمراد بالأحسن وجهاً أكثر صلاة بالليل. (فتح)
And the most knowledgeable [i.e., of the rulings of prayer if he knows the amount of recitation obligatory. (Fath)] i.e., the most knowledgeable of what corrects and invalidates prayer, provided he knows from recitation the amount that fulfills the sunnah of recitation. Abu Yusuf said: The best reciter is more entitled, acting upon the apparent meaning of what is in the Sahih: 'Let the one who recites the Book of Allah best lead the people; if they are equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah; if equal in the Sunnah, then the earliest in emigration; if equal in emigration, then the earliest in Islam.' And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Order Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer,' and there was present one who was a better reciter than him, as evidenced by what was narrated: 'The best reciter among you is Ubayy.' So the only remaining [reason] is that he was the most knowledgeable. And the best reciter was given precedence in the hadith because they used to learn the Qur'an with its rulings. It is reported from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he memorized Surat al-Baqarah in twelve years, and Ibn 'Umar said: 'No surah was revealed except that we knew its commands, prohibitions, warnings, lawful, and unlawful.' Thus, being the best reciter necessarily implies being the most knowledgeable. Appendix: Among the Companions who memorized the Qur'an were Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Zaid ibn Thabit, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Abu Zaid al-Ansari, 'Uthman ibn 'Affan; and there is a difference regarding Abu al-Darda', 'Ubadah, and Tamim al-Dari. (Fath)
Then the most pious, then the oldest in age. And it is disliked for a slave, a Bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, a child of fornication to lead, and prolonging prayer. Due to people's aversion to him.
Then the most pious: i.e., one who guards against ambiguous things; due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'If you want your prayer to be accepted, let your best ones lead you, for they are your delegates between you and your Lord.' And because they gave precedence to the earliest in emigration, but there is no emigration today, so we placed the most pious in its stead. The majority follow giving precedence to the most pious over the oldest, contrary to what is in 'al-Muhit'. (Fath) The oldest: due to his statement to Malik ibn Huwairith and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, give the call and establish it, and let the older of you lead.' And because giving precedence to the oldest increases the congregation. If they are equal in age, then the one with the best appearance, or the best character and conduct; if equal, the most noble in lineage; if equal, they cast lots. If they give precedence to other than the most deserving, they do wrong without sin. If a man leads a people while they dislike him due to some defect in him, or because someone else there is more entitled to the imamate, it is prohibitively disliked for him; due to the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads a people while they are averse to him.' And the meaning of 'best appearance' is more prayer at night. (Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications for who is most deserving to lead congregational prayer. The matn states: the most knowledgeable (a‘lam) is most entitled, then the best reciter (aqra’), then the most pious (awra‘), then the oldest (asann). The commentary elaborates that 'a‘lam' means knowledge of the rulings of prayer, even if the imam only knows the minimum recitation. Abu Yusuf disagreed, preferring the best reciter based on the hadith, 'The best reciter should lead.' The authors of the sharh (the Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, though they usually agree, here they support Abu Hanifa) argue that the hadith ordering Abu Bakr to lead, though he was not the best reciter (Ubayy was), shows that knowledge was the real criterion. The hadith prioritizing recitation is interpreted in light of the fact that the Companions learned the Qur'an with its meanings, so the best reciter was also the most knowledgeable. Then the passage explains the next two criteria: the most pious (who avoids doubtful matters) and the oldest (to respect age and increase congregation). If equal in age, other factors like appearance, character, lineage, and lot are considered. The passage also notes that if someone leads while people dislike him, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to a hadith. This section sets a detailed protocol for selecting an imam to ensure community harmony.

Key Terms
الأعلم (al-a‘lam): The most knowledgeable in matters that affect the validity of prayer (fiqh al-salah).
الأقرأ (al-aqra’): The best reciter of the Qur'an.
الأورع (al-awra‘): The most pious, one who avoids doubtful matters (shubuhāt).
الأسن (al-asann): The oldest in age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, who is most deserving to lead prayer?
A) The best reciter (aqra’)
B) The most knowledgeable (a‘lam)
C) The most pious (awra‘)
D) The oldest (asann)

Key Takeaway
The most knowledgeable person (a‘lam) is the most deserving to lead prayer, even if another is a better reciter.

Disliked Imams: Who Should Not Lead
Lists disliked imams and explains reasons with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories of imams whose leadership is disliked in the Hanafi school and state whether the prayer is valid or invalid in each case.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a sinful person is valid but disliked; behind an innovator of kufr it is invalid.

The Hanafi school emphasizes that congregational prayer should be led by someone who is competent and avoids causing aversion. This lesson examines the specific categories of individuals whose imamate is considered disliked (makruh) and the reasoning behind each ruling, including the important distinction between innovations that do and do not amount to disbelief. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for selecting an appropriate imam in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify each category
List the six categories mentioned in the matn: slave, Bedouin, sinful person, innovator, blind person, and child of fornication. Include the additional ruling on prolonging prayer.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For each category, state whether the imamate is valid or invalid and at which level of dislike (tanzihi or tahrimi). Note the exceptions: learned Bedouin, blind person if best available, and the kufr innovator.
The innovator distinction is key: non-kufr innovation is disliked, kufr innovation makes imamate invalid.
3
Analyse the evidence
For the sinful person, note the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' For prolonging prayer, note the hadith of the Prophet ordering lightness and the incident of Mu'adh.
4
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute
Malik holds that prayer behind a sinful person is invalid; the Hanafi response is that it is permissible but disliked based on the hadith.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider how these rulings apply today: e.g., an imam who prolongs prayer excessively, or a person with tattoos (sinful) leading prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة . لنفره الناس عنه

والأعرابي [ أي ساكن البادية عربياً أو عجمياً للحنه وجهله. (ع)] منسوب إلى الأعراب، بفتح الهمزة من أوزان الجمع لا واحد له، وليس جمع العرب، وهو البدوي، كره إمامته لبعده عن مجالس العلم كما حكي أن أعرابيا اقتدى بإمام في صلاة المغرب وقرأ الإمام الأَعْرَابُ أَشَدُّ كُفْراً وَنِفَاقا (التوبة: ٩٧) فلما سمع الأعرابي انصرف وأخذ عصا وضرب به على كتف الإمام، ثم اقتدى ثانيا وقرأ الإمام: ﴿وَمِنَ الْأَعْرَابِ مَنْ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ﴾ (التوبة:٩٩) فقال الأعرابي وهو في الصلاة: "قد نفعك العصا"، فهذا يدل على غالب جهلهم فإن كان عالماً تقياً فهو كغيره ويستحب تقديمه (فتح مستخلص) والفاسق: فإن قدموه جاز؛ لقوله عليها: "صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر"، وكراهة إمامته؛ لأنه لا يهتم بأمر دينه؛ ولأن في تقديمه تقليل الجماعة، وقال مالك: لا تجوز الصلاة خلفه. ( فتح، مستخلص) والمبتدع أي صاحب بدعة لا يكفر بها كمن ينكر الرؤية، بخلاف صاحب البدعة المكفرة كمن ينكر خلافة الصديق فلا تصح إمامة الرافضي والجهمي والقدري كذلك. (ط،ع) والأعمى: لأنه لا يتوقى النجاسة، وفي "البدائع": وإذا كان لا يوازيه غيره في الفضيلة فهو أولى، وقد استخلف النبي عليه ابن أم مكتوم على المدينة. رمز الحقائق: ٦٥/١] وولد الزنا : لنفرة الناس عنه لكونه متهماً. (ع) وتطويل الصلاة [ أي كره للإمام تطويل الصلاة على القوم زيادة على قدر السنة تحريماً لحديث معاذ. (ط،ع)] لقوله : " من أمّ قوماً فليصل بهم صلاة أضعفهم؛ فإن فيهم المريض والكبير وذا الحاجة"، وكذا أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر حين سمع بكاء صبي، فلما فرغ قالوا له: أو جزت؟ قال: "سمعت بكاء صبي أن تفتتن أمه، والظاهر أن الكراهة في تطويل الصلاة تحريمية؛ للأمر بالتخفيف واستثنى صلاة الكسوف؛ فإن
صح
عنه
فخشیت
السنة فيها التطويل حتى تنجلي الشمس، ولا فرق في قراءة التطويل بين القراءة والتسبيحات وغيرها. (فتح)
And it is disliked for a slave, a Bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, a child of fornication to lead, and prolonging prayer. Due to people's aversion to him.

The Bedouin: i.e., a dweller of the desert, Arab or non-Arab, due to his incorrect speech and ignorance. (Ayni) It is ascribed to 'a'rab' (Bedouins), with fatha on the hamza, a plural form with no singular, and it is not the plural of 'arab. He is a desert dweller. His imamate is disliked because of his distance from gatherings of knowledge. As it is narrated that a Bedouin followed an imam in Maghrib prayer and the imam recited 'The Bedouins are stronger in disbelief and hypocrisy' (9:97). When the Bedouin heard that, he left, took a stick, and struck it on the imam's shoulder. Then he followed again, and the imam recited 'And among the Bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' (9:99). So the Bedouin said while in prayer: 'The stick has benefited you.' This indicates their general ignorance. If he is knowledgeable and pious, he is like others, and it is recommended to give him precedence. (Fath, Mukhtasar) The sinful person: if they give him precedence, it is permissible due to his statement: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' And his imamate is disliked because he does not care about his religion, and because giving him precedence reduces the congregation. Malik said: Prayer behind him is not valid. (Fath, Mukhtasar) The innovator: i.e., one who holds an innovation that does not render him a disbeliever, like one who denies the vision [of Allah]. As opposed to one who holds an innovation that is disbelief, like one who denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr. So the imamate of a Rafidi, a Jahmi, and a Qadari is not valid. (Tahawi, Ayni) The blind person: because he does not avoid impurity. In al-Bada'i': if there is no one equal to him in virtue, he is more entitled. The Prophet appointed Ibn Umm Maktum over Medina. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 65/1) The child of fornication: due to people's aversion to him because he is suspected. (Ayni) Prolonging prayer: i.e., it is disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer over the people beyond the sunnah, prohibitively disliked (tahriman) due to the hadith of Mu'adh. (Tahawi, Ayni) Due to his statement: 'Whoever leads a people should lead them in the prayer of the weakest among them; for among them are the sick, the old, and the one with need.' Similarly, he recited the Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr when he heard a child crying; when he finished, they said: 'Did you shorten it?' He said: 'I heard a child crying, fearing his mother may be tempted.' And the apparent is that the dislike for prolonging prayer is prohibitive, due to the command to lighten, except the eclipse prayer, for the sunnah in it is prolongation until the sun clears. There is no difference in prolonging prayer between recitation, tasbihat, and others. (Fath)
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage lists individuals whose imamate is disliked (makruh) and explains the reasons. The matn states: it is disliked for a slave, a Bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, a child of fornication, and also it is disliked to prolong prayer. The commentary elaborates: The Bedouin is disliked due to his ignorance and potential lack of proper pronunciation; a story illustrates the typical ignorance of Bedouins. However, if he is learned and pious, he is like others. The sinful person (fasiq) is disliked because he does not care about religion, but it is still impermissible to pray behind him? Actually, the text says it is permissible (jāz) but disliked; Malik said it is invalid. The innovator (mubtadi') with an innovation that does not amount to kufr (like denying ru'yat Allah) is disliked; but if the innovation is kufr (like Rafidi who abuses the Sahaba), his imamate is invalid. The blind person is disliked because he cannot avoid impurity, but if he is the best available, it is allowed; the Prophet had Ibn Umm Maktum lead. The child of fornication (walad al-zinā) is disliked due to social stigma. Prolonging prayer (taṭwīl al-ṣalāh) beyond the sunnah is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because the Prophet ordered lightness, except for eclipse prayer where prolongation is sunnah. This section encourages selecting an imam who is competent and considerate, avoiding those who may cause harm or aversion.

Key Terms
الأعرابي (al-a‘rābī): A Bedouin, a desert dweller, often characterized by ignorance of proper Islamic practices.
المبتدع (al-mubtadi‘): One who holds an innovative belief (bid'ah) that does not amount to disbelief, e.g., denying the vision of Allah.
تطويل الصلاة (taṭwīl al-ṣalāh): Prolonging the prayer beyond the sunnah, which is disliked due to hardship on followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying behind a sinful person (fasiq)?
A) The prayer is invalid
B) The prayer is valid but disliked
C) The prayer is invalid and sinful
D) The prayer is recommended

Key Takeaway
Most disliked imams render the prayer valid but inferior; the exception is the innovator of kufr, whose imamate is invalid.

Precedence in Imamate: The Most Pious Then the Oldest
Ruling with proof on order of imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of precedence for selecting an imam and justify why piety (al-awra') is prioritized over age (al-asan) using hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The most pious should lead the prayer; age is secondary.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the order of precedence for selecting an imam. The Hanafi school prioritizes piety (al-awra') over age (al-asan), based on prophetic hadith and analogy with the earlier practice of prioritizing emigration (hijra). The majority of Hanafi scholars follow this order, though a minority view in al-Muhit gives precedence to age.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The text states: 'Then the most pious (al-awra'), then the oldest (al-asan).' This is the preferred order for selecting an imam.
The ruling is that this order is recommended (sunnah), not obligatory.
2
Locate the proofs for piety
The hadith: 'If you are pleased that Allah accepts your prayer, then let your best ones lead you...' supports giving precedence to the most pious. Also, the analogy with hijra: earlier, precedence was given to those who emigrated earliest; now, piety takes its place.
The phrase 'best ones' is interpreted as the most cautious in avoiding unlawful matters.
3
Locate the proofs for age
The hadith to Malik ibn Huwairith: 'let the older of you lead you' supports consideration of age. Also, giving precedence to the oldest may increase the congregation.
The Hanafi school harmonizes these by placing piety first, then age.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference
The majority (al-akthar) give piety precedence, contrary to what is in al-Muhit, which gives age precedence. The commentator sides with the majority.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is piety first.
5
Apply when candidates are equal
If equal in piety and age, then consider beauty of face (interpreted as much night prayer), character, lineage, and finally draw lots. If the congregation appoints someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong but without sin.
Drawing lots is a last resort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأورع ثم الأسن، وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة . لنفره الناس عنه ثم الأورع: أي المحترز عن شبهة الحرام؛ لقوله عليه: "إن سركم أن يتقبل الله صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم، فإنهم وفدكم أي رسلكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم"؛ ولأنه عليها قدم أقدمهم هجرة ولا هجرة اليوم، فأقمنا الأورع مقامها، وعلى تقديم الأورع على الأسن جرى الأكثر عكس ما في "المحيط". (فتح) الأسن: لقوله لمالك بن حويرث ولصاحب له : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا ثم أقيما وليؤمكما أكبر كما"؛ ولأن في تقديم الأسن تكثير الجماعة، فإن كانوا في السن سواء فأحسنهم وجهاً أو أحسنهم خلقا ومعاشرة، فإن كانوا سواء فأشرفهم نسبا، فإن تساووا يقرع بينهم، ولو قدموا غير الأولى أساءوا بلا إثم، ولو أم قوماً وهم له كارهون لفساد فيه، أو لأن غيره هناك أحق بالإمامة منه كره له ذلك تحريماً؛ لحديث أبي داود: "لا يقبل الله صلاة من تقدم قوماً وهم له كارهون، والمراد بالأحسن وجهاً أكثر صلاة بالليل. (فتح) والأعرابي [ أي ساكن البادية عربياً أو عجمياً للحنه وجهله. (ع)] منسوب إلى الأعراب، بفتح الهمزة من أوزان الجمع لا واحد له، وليس جمع العرب، وهو البدوي، كره إمامته لبعده عن مجالس العلم كما حكي أن أعرابيا اقتدى بإمام في صلاة المغرب وقرأ الإمام الأَعْرَابُ أَشَدُّ كُفْراً وَنِفَاقا (التوبة: ٩٧) فلما سمع الأعرابي انصرف وأخذ عصا وضرب به على كتف الإمام، ثم اقتدى ثانيا وقرأ الإمام: ﴿وَمِنَ الْأَعْرَابِ مَنْ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ﴾ (التوبة:٩٩) فقال الأعرابي وهو في الصلاة: "قد نفعك العصا"، فهذا يدل على غالب جهلهم فإن كان عالماً تقياً فهو كغيره ويستحب تقديمه (فتح مستخلص) والفاسق: فإن قدموه جاز؛ لقوله عليها: "صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر"، وكراهة إمامته؛ لأنه لا يهتم بأمر دينه؛ ولأن في تقديمه تقليل الجماعة، وقال مالك: لا تجوز الصلاة خلفه. ( فتح، مستخلص) والمبتدع أي صاحب بدعة لا يكفر بها كمن ينكر الرؤية، بخلاف صاحب البدعة المكفرة كمن ينكر خلافة الصديق فلا تصح إمامة الرافضي والجهمي والقدري كذلك. (ط،ع) والأعمى: لأنه لا يتوقى النجاسة، وفي "البدائع": وإذا كان لا يوازيه غيره في الفضيلة فهو أولى، وقد استخلف النبي عليه ابن أم مكتوم على المدينة. رمز الحقائق: ٦٥/١] وولد الزنا : لنفرة الناس عنه لكونه متهماً. (ع) وتطويل الصلاة [ أي كره للإمام تطويل الصلاة على القوم زيادة على قدر السنة تحريماً لحديث معاذ. (ط،ع)] لقوله : " من أمّ قوماً فليصل بهم صلاة أضعفهم؛ فإن فيهم المريض والكبير وذا الحاجة"، وكذا أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر حين سمع بكاء صبي، فلما فرغ قالوا له: أو جزت؟ قال: "سمعت بكاء صبي أن تفتتن أمه، والظاهر أن الكراهة في تطويل الصلاة تحريمية؛ للأمر بالتخفيف واستثنى صلاة الكسوف؛ فإن صح عنه فخشیت السنة فيها التطويل حتى تنجلي الشمس، ولا فرق في قراءة التطويل بين القراءة والتسبيحات وغيرها. (فتح)
Then the most pious, then the oldest. And it is disliked (to appoint) as imam: a slave, a bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, an illegitimate child, and prolonging the prayer. -Due to people's aversion from him- Then the most pious: meaning the one who avoids doubtful matters regarding the unlawful; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'If you are pleased that Allah accepts your prayer, then let your best ones lead you, for they are your delegates (representatives) between you and your Lord.' And because he (peace be upon him) used to give precedence to the one with the earliest emigration, and there is no emigration today, so we have placed the most pious in its place. And the majority act upon giving precedence to the most pious over the oldest, contrary to what is in al-Muhit. (Fath) The oldest: due to his saying to Malik ibn Huwairith and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, call the adhan and iqama, and let the older of you lead you.' And because giving precedence to the oldest increases the congregation. If they are equal in age, then the best in face (i.e., most night prayer), or the best in character and social behavior. If they are equal, then the noblest in lineage. If they are equal, they draw lots. If they appoint someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong without sin. If a person leads a people while they are averse to him - due to corruption in him, or because someone else is more entitled to leadership than him - it is prohibitively disliked for him to do so, due to the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads a people while they are averse to him.' And what is meant by 'best in face' is one who prays more at night. (Fath) And al-A'rabi: meaning a dweller of the desert, Arab or non-Arab, due to his poor Arabic and ignorance. It is attributed to al-A'rab, with fatha on the hamza, a plural pattern without a singular, and it is not the plural of Arab; it is the Bedouin. It is disliked for him to lead due to his distance from the circles of knowledge, as narrated that a Bedouin followed an imam in Maghrib prayer, and the imam recited: 'The Bedouins are the most severe in disbelief and hypocrisy' (9:97). When the Bedouin heard that, he left and took a stick and struck the imam on his shoulder. Then he followed again and the imam recited: 'And among the Bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' (9:99). The Bedouin said while in prayer: 'The stick has benefited you.' This indicates their prevalent ignorance. But if he is a knowledgeable and pious person, he is like anyone else, and it is recommended to give him precedence. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And the sinful person: if they appoint him, it is permissible; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' And it is disliked for him to lead because he does not care about his religious affairs, and because giving him precedence reduces the congregation. Malik said: 'Prayer behind him is not permissible.' (Fath, Mustakhlas) And the innovator: meaning one who holds an innovation that does not render him a disbeliever, like one who denies the vision (of Allah in the afterlife). As for one whose innovation is excommunicating (takfir), like one who denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, his leadership is not valid - similarly the Rafidi, Jahmi, and Qadari. (T, A) And the blind person: because he does not avoid impurity. In al-Bada'i': 'If no one else matches him in excellence, he is more deserving.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed Ibn Umm Maktum as his deputy over Medina. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/65) And the illegitimate child: due to people's aversion to him because he is suspect. (A) And prolonging the prayer: meaning it is prohibitively disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer upon the people beyond the amount of the sunna, due to the hadith of Muadh. (T, A) Due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever leads a people should pray with them the prayer of the weakest among them, for among them are the sick, the elderly, and the one with a need.' And likewise, he recited the Mu'awwidhatain in Fajr when he heard a child crying, and when he finished they said to him: 'Did you believe?' He said: 'I heard the cry of a child fearing that his mother would be tempted.' And it appears that the dislike for prolonging the prayer is prohibitively so, due to the command to lighten, and he excepted the eclipse prayer, for it is established from him that he feared (?) the sunna in it is prolongation until the sun clears. And there is no difference in prolonging prayer between recitation, tasbihat, and other things. (Fath)
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the rules of imamate (leadership in prayer). It begins by stating the preferred order: the most pious (al-awra') should be given precedence, then the oldest (al-asan). This is based on hadith evidence. The commentator explains that 'al-awra' refers to one who avoids doubtful matters, and this takes the place of the earlier practice of giving precedence based on precedence in emigration (hijra), which is no longer applicable. The majority prefer the pious over the older, though there is a contrary view in al-Muhit. Then the text lists individuals whose imamate is disliked (makruh): a slave, a bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, an illegitimate child, and the act of prolonging the prayer. For each, the commentator provides proofs and sometimes additional details. For example, the bedouin is disliked because of his ignorance and lack of familiarity with Islamic knowledge, but if he is knowledgeable and pious, it is recommended to give him precedence. The sinful person (fasiq): his imamate is valid but disliked, and the text notes that Imam Malik holds it invalid - this is an inter-madhhab difference. The innovator (mubtadi'): innovation that does not amount to disbelief (like denying the vision of Allah) results in dislike, but innovation that is kufr (like denying Abu Bakr's caliphate) renders the imamate invalid. The blind person's imamate is disliked because he cannot avoid impurity, but if he is the best qualified, it is fine - the Prophet himself appointed a blind companion as governor. The illegitimate child is disliked due to public aversion. Prolonging the prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) beyond the sunna amount, based on the hadith of lightening the prayer and the example of the Prophet shortening his recitation upon hearing a child cry. The passage underscores that the imamate should be a means of drawing people together, not repelling them.

Key Terms
الأورع (al-awra'): The most cautious about doubtful matters, the most pious.
الأسن (al-asan): The older in age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first criterion for selecting an imam?
A) Age
B) Knowledge
C) Piety (al-awra')
D) Lineage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the most pious person should lead the prayer, followed by the oldest; deviating from this order is disliked but the prayer is valid.

Disliked Imams: Rulings on Who May Lead with Disapproval
Ruling with proof on disliked imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories of imams whose imamate is disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school, explain the proofs and exceptions for each, and state the Hanafi view on the validity of prayer behind a fasiq in contrast to the Maliki school.

Core Idea
The imamate of certain individuals is valid but disliked; the prayer is valid but sinful to appoint them.

This passage lists several categories of imams whose leadership is considered disliked (makruh) but whose prayer is still valid. The Hanafi school distinguishes between validity and desirability, and the text provides proofs from hadith and logic for each category. Notable is the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik, who holds prayer behind a fasiq to be invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of disliked imams
The text begins by stating it is disliked to appoint as imam: a slave, a bedouin, a sinful person (fasiq), an innovator (mubtadi'), a blind person, and an illegitimate child (walad al-zina).
The list is not exhaustive; it also includes prolonging prayer, which is covered in a separate lesson.
2
Examine the proof for each category
For the bedouin: a story illustrates their ignorance, but if knowledgeable, he is like anyone else. For the fasiq: the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person' permits validity, but dislike is due to lack of religious concern and reduction of congregation. For the innovator: distinction between innovation not reaching kufr (disliked) and innovation that is kufr (invalidates). For the blind: because he cannot avoid impurity, but if he is the best, he may lead. For the illegitimate child: due to public aversion.
Each proof is specific; note exceptions.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute on the fasiq
Imam Malik holds that prayer behind a fasiq is invalid. The Hanafi school holds it valid but disliked, based on the hadith and the principle that the imam's sin does not affect the follower.
This is a key khilaf that affects practice.
4
Apply the ruling on validity with dislike
If a person from these categories leads the prayer, the prayer of the followers is valid, but it is sinful for the congregation to appoint him. However, if they did so, they have done wrong without sin? The text says 'أساءوا بلا إثم' (they do wrong without sin) in the context of appointing a non-preferred imam. For these categories, the ruling is similar: the act of appointment is disliked but not sinful? The text says 'كره إمامة' which implies karaha. The commentator explains that the imamate itself is valid but disliked.
The degree of karaha may vary; leading when disliked is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) for the imam.

Then the most pious, then the oldest. And because he (peace be upon him) used to give precedence to the one with the earliest emigration, and there is no emigration today, so we have placed the most pious in its place. And the majority act upon giving precedence to the most pious over the oldest, contrary to what is in al-Muhit. (Fath) The oldest: due to his saying to Malik ibn Huwairith and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, call the adhan and iqama, and let the older of you lead you.' And because giving precedence to the oldest increases the congregation. If they are equal in age, then the best in face (i.e., most night prayer), or the best in character and social behavior. If they are equal, then the noblest in lineage. If they are equal, they draw lots. If they appoint someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong without sin. If a person leads a people while they are averse to him - due to corruption in him, or because someone else is more entitled to leadership than him - it is prohibitively disliked for him to do so, due to the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads a people while they are averse to him.' And what is meant by 'best in face' is one who prays more at night. (Fath) And al-A'rabi: meaning a dweller of the desert, Arab or non-Arab, due to his poor Arabic and ignorance. It is attributed to al-A'rab, with fatha on the hamza, a plural pattern without a singular, and it is not the plural of Arab; it is the Bedouin. It is disliked for him to lead due to his distance from the circles of knowledge, as narrated that a Bedouin followed an imam in Maghrib prayer, and the imam recited: 'The Bedouins are the most severe in disbelief and hypocrisy' (9:97). When the Bedouin heard that, he left and took a stick and struck the imam on his shoulder. Then he followed again and the imam recited: 'And among the Bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' (9:99). The Bedouin said while in prayer: 'The stick has benefited you.' This indicates their prevalent ignorance. But if he is a knowledgeable and pious person, he is like anyone else, and it is recommended to give him precedence. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And the sinful person: if they appoint him, it is permissible; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' And it is disliked for him to lead because he does not care about his religious affairs, and because giving him precedence reduces the congregation. Malik said: 'Prayer behind him is not permissible.' (Fath, Mustakhlas) And the innovator: meaning one who holds an innovation that does not render him a disbeliever, like one who denies the vision (of Allah in the afterlife). As for one whose innovation is excommunicating (takfir), like one who denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, his leadership is not valid - similarly the Rafidi, Jahmi, and Qadari. (T, A) And the blind person: because he does not avoid impurity. In al-Bada'i': 'If no one else matches him in excellence, he is more deserving.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed Ibn Umm Maktum as his deputy over Medina. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/65) And the illegitimate child: due to people's aversion to him because he is suspect. (A) And prolonging the prayer: meaning it is prohibitively disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer upon the people beyond the amount of the sunna, due to the hadith of Muadh. (T, A) Due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever leads a people should pray with them the prayer of the weakest among them, for among them are the sick, the elderly, and the one with a need.' And likewise, he recited the Mu'awwidhatain in Fajr when he heard a child crying, and when he finished they said to him: 'Did you believe?' He said: 'I heard the cry of a child fearing that his mother would be tempted.' And it appears that the dislike for prolonging the prayer is prohibitively so, due to the command to lighten, and he excepted the eclipse prayer, for it is established from him that he feared (?) the sunna in it is prolongation until the sun clears. And there is no difference in prolonging prayer between recitation, tasbihat, and other things. (Fath)
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the rules of imamate (leadership in prayer). It begins by stating the preferred order: the most pious (al-awra') should be given precedence, then the oldest (al-asan). This is based on hadith evidence. The commentator explains that 'al-awra' refers to one who avoids doubtful matters, and this takes the place of the earlier practice of giving precedence based on precedence in emigration (hijra), which is no longer applicable. The majority prefer the pious over the older, though there is a contrary view in al-Muhit. Then the text lists individuals whose imamate is disliked (makruh): a slave, a bedouin, a sinful person, an innovator, a blind person, an illegitimate child, and the act of prolonging the prayer. For each, the commentator provides proofs and sometimes additional details. For example, the bedouin is disliked because of his ignorance and lack of familiarity with Islamic knowledge, but if he is knowledgeable and pious, it is recommended to give him precedence. The sinful person (fasiq): his imamate is valid but disliked, and the text notes that Imam Malik holds it invalid - this is an inter-madhhab difference. The innovator (mubtadi'): innovation that does not amount to disbelief (like denying the vision of Allah) results in dislike, but innovation that is kufr (like denying Abu Bakr's caliphate) renders the imamate invalid. The blind person's imamate is disliked because he cannot avoid impurity, but if he is the best qualified, it is fine - the Prophet himself appointed a blind companion as governor. The illegitimate child is disliked due to public aversion. Prolonging the prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) beyond the sunna amount, based on the hadith of lightening the prayer and the example of the Prophet shortening his recitation upon hearing a child cry. The passage underscores that the imamate should be a means of drawing people together, not repelling them.

Key Terms
الأعرابي (al-a'rabi): A Bedouin, often ignorant of Islamic rulings.
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A sinful person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.
المبتدع (al-mubtadi'): An innovator; distinction between non-takfiri (disliked) and takfiri (invalid).
الأعمى (al-a'ma): A blind person; imamate disliked due to inability to avoid impurity, but if best, recommended.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): An illegitimate child; imamate disliked due to public aversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the imamate of a person who denies the vision of Allah (ru'ya)?
A) Invalid because it is kufr.
B) Valid but disliked because it is a non-takfiri innovation.
C) Valid and not disliked.
D) Invalid only if he is a Rafidi.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the imamate of a slave, bedouin, fasiq, non-takfiri innovator, blind person, and illegitimate child is valid but disliked; the prayer is valid except when the innovation amounts to kufr.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Prohibition of Prolonging Prayer in Congregation
Ruling with proof on prolonging prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on an imam prolonging the prayer beyond the sunna and identify the evidence and exception for the eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer beyond the sunna is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for the imam.

This passage addresses the imam's duty to lighten the prayer out of consideration for the congregation. Prolonging beyond the sunna amount is strongly disliked, based on the hadith of the Prophet instructing to pray with the weakest in mind. An exception is made for the eclipse prayer, where prolongation is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on prolonging prayer
The text states 'and prolonging the prayer' is disliked. The commentator clarifies that it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for the imam to prolong the prayer beyond the amount of the sunna.
This applies to obligatory prayers; sunna prayers are not covered.
2
Examine the proof
The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever leads a people should pray with them the prayer of the weakest among them, for among them are the sick, the elderly, and the one with a need.' Also, the Prophet shortened his recitation upon hearing a child cry.
The hadith gives clear instruction to lighten.
3
Note the exception for eclipse prayer
The text excepts the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf), because the sunna is to prolong it until the sun clears.
This is a special case due to the nature of the prayer.
4
Clarify the scope of prolonging
The prohibition applies to all forms of prolonging: recitation, tasbihat (subha), and other acts. There is no distinction.
This ensures that the imam does not burden the congregation in any way.

Source Text

ثم الأورع ثم الأسن، وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة . لنفره الناس عنه ثم الأورع: أي المحترز عن شبهة الحرام؛ لقوله عليه: "إن سركم أن يتقبل الله صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم، فإنهم وفدكم أي رسلكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم"؛ ولأنه عليها قدم أقدمهم هجرة ولا هجرة اليوم، فأقمنا الأورع مقامها، وعلى تقديم الأورع على الأسن جرى الأكثر عكس ما في "المحيط". beginner
