Ruling on Women's Congregation in Prayer
Ruling with proof for women's congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregation and explain why it is makruh tahrimi, citing the hadith and the 'illa of the imam's position.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is prohibitively disliked because the imam must stand in the middle, abandoning the wajib of being forward.

This lesson examines the ruling on women praying in congregation. While men's congregation is highly recommended, the Hanafi school considers women's congregation to be makruh tahrimi. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being ruled upon: women praying in congregation. State the ruling: it is makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited in the text: the hadith that a woman's prayer in her house is better than in her courtyard, and in her private chamber better than in her house.
This hadith indicates the superiority of individual prayer at home over congregation.
3
Understand the 'illa
Identify the effective cause for the dislike: women's congregation necessitates the imam standing in the middle of the row, which either abandons the wajib of the imam being forward or increases exposure.
The same 'illa applies to the congregation of naked persons.
4
Note the analogy with the naked
Recognize that the congregation of naked persons is also makruh tahrimi due to the same necessary consequence.
This strengthens the ruling by qiyas.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that women's congregation is makruh tahrimi; if they do it, the imam stands in the middle.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجماعة النساء، فإن فعلن تقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة، ويقف الواحد عن يمينه والاثنان خلفه، ويصفُ الرُّجال . أي كره تحريماً أيضاً وحدهن أي الإمام أي يقف الإمام وجماعة النساء لقوله علي : صلاة المرأة في بيتها أفضل من صلاتها في حجرتها، وصلاتها في مخدعها أفضل من صلاتها في بيتها؛ ولأن جماعتهن وحدهن لا تخلو عن ارتكاب محرم، وهو وقوف الإمام وسط الصف. (فتح) فإن فعلن أي فإن أردن أن يصلين بجماعة (ط) وسطهن أي إن صلين بالجماعة مع كراهتها تقف الإمام وسطهن؛ لأن عائشة مهما فعلت كذلك، وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الإسلام ولأن في التقديم زيادة الكشف، ولا بد من تقدم عقب الإمام عن عقب من خلفها. (فتح، مستخلص) كالعراة: [ أي كما يقف إمام العراة وسطهم تحرزاً عن زيادة الكشف (ط)] جمع عار من الثوب، وفيه إيماء إلى كراهة جماعة العراة أيضاً كراهة تحريم؛ لاتحاد اللازم، وهو إما ترك واجب التقدم، أو زيادة الكشف. (فتح) ويقف الواحد إلخ ولو صبياً يعقل عنه يمينه بلا فرجة؛ لأنه عليها صلى بابن عباس هما فأقامه عن يمينه، وعن محمد أنه يضع أصابعه عند عقب الإمام، والعبرة لموضع الوقوف لا لموضع السجود حتى لو كان المقتدي أطول من الإمام فوقع سجوده أمام الإمام لم يضره، وقوله: "عن يمينه" قيد للفضيلة حتى لو صلى في يساره أو خلفه جاز ويكون مسيئاً لمخالفة السنة. [ رمز الحقائق: ٦٦/١] يمينه : أي المقتدي الواحد عن يمين الإمام مساوياً له لا متأخر عنه . (ط، ع) والاثنان خلفه وعن أبي يوسف أنه يتوسطهما؛ لأن ابن مسعود لما صلى بعلقمة والأسود في بيته وقام وسطهما، ولهما: أنه عليه صلى بأنس ويتيم فأقامهما خلفه وأم سليم وراءهما، وفعل ابن مسعود ما كان لضيق المقام، كذا قال النخعي، وهو أعلم الناس مذهب ابن مسعود والمرأة في حكم الاصطفاف كالعدم حتى لو كان خلفه رجل واحد وامرأة يقوم الرجل بحذائه كما لو لم يكن امرأة، وإن كثر القوم كره قيام الإمام وسطهم تحريماً لترك الواجب أي التقدم [ رمز الحقائق: ٦٦/١] (فتح) ويصف الرجال: أي صف الرجال مقدم على صف الصبيان وهو مقدم على صف الخناثي، وهو مقدم على صف النساء؛ لقوله : "ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى". [ تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٠/١] وينبغي للقوم أن يتراصوا ويسدوا الخلل ويسووا بين مناكبهم في الصفوف، ولا بأس أن يأمرهم الإمام بذلك لقوله عليه: "سووا صفوفكم؛ فإن تسوية الصفوف من تمام الصلاة"، وقال علي: لتسون صفوفكم أو ليخالفن الله بين وجوهكم" وهو راجع إلى اختلاف القلوب، وينبغي للإمام أن يقف بإزاء الوسط فإن لم يفعل فقد أساء، وينبغي أن يكملوا الصف الأول حتى إذا وجد فرجة فيه دون الثاني له أن يخرق الثاني؛ إذ لا حرمة لهم لتقصيرهم حيث لم يسدوا الصف الأول ثم يكمل ما يليه، وهلم جرا ، قال : "أقيموا الصفوف وحاذوا بين المناكب وسدوا الخلل ولينوا بأيدي إخوانكم ولا تذروا فرجات الشيطان من وصل صفاً وصله الله ومن قطع صفا قطعه الله"، وقال: "خياركم ألينكم مناكب في الصلاة". (فتح)
And (the chapter of) the congregation of women. If they do it, the imam stands in their middle like (the imam of) the naked. And one (follower) stands on his right, and two behind him, and the men arrange in rows. - Meaning it is also prohibitively disliked for them (to gather) alone? (?) The imam and the congregation of women: due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her courtyard, and her prayer in her private chamber is better than her prayer in her house.' And because their congregation alone involves committing a forbidden act, which is the imam standing in the middle of the row. (Fath) If they do it: meaning if they want to pray in congregation (T) in their middle: i.e., if they pray in congregation despite its dislike, the imam stands in their middle, because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did so, and her action is interpreted as in early Islam. And because putting him in front increases exposure. And the imam's heel must be ahead of the heels of those behind her. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Like the naked: (meaning just as the imam of the naked stands in their middle to avoid increased exposure - T) a plural of 'aryan (naked). And it implies that the congregation of the naked is also prohibitively disliked, because the same necessary consequence applies, which is either leaving the obligatory forward position or increasing exposure. (Fath) And one (follower) stands etc., even if a discerning boy, on his right without a gap; because he (peace be upon him) prayed with Ibn Abbas (?) and placed him on his right. And from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani) that he places his fingers at the level of the imam's heel. And the consideration is for the place of standing, not the place of prostration; even if the follower is taller than the imam and his prostration occurs in front of the imam, it does not harm him. And his saying: 'on his right' is a condition of virtue; even if he prays on his left or behind him, it is permissible but he is doing wrong by violating the sunna. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/66] His right: meaning the individual follower stands on the right of the imam, level with him, not behind him. (T, A) And two behind him: And from Abu Yusuf that he (the imam) stands between them, because Ibn Mas'ud prayed with Alqama and al-Aswad in his house and stood between them. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that he (peace be upon him) prayed with Anas and an orphan and placed them behind him, and Umm Sulaym behind them. And Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to narrowness of space, as al-Nakha'i said, and he is the most knowledgeable of the people regarding Ibn Mas'ud's school. And a woman is as if nonexistent in the ranks: even if behind him there is one man and one woman, the man stands parallel to him as if there were no woman. And if the people are many, it is prohibitively disliked for the imam to stand in their middle because of abandoning the wajib, i.e., being forward. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/66] (Fath) And the men arrange in rows: meaning the row of men precedes the row of boys, which precedes the row of hermaphrodites (khunatha), which precedes the row of women; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible (ulu al-ahlam wal-nuha) be nearest to me.' [Tabyin al-Haqaiq: 1/350] And it is recommended for the people to stand shoulder to shoulder, fill the gaps, and align their shoulders in the rows. And it is fine for the imam to command them to do so, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Straighten your rows, for straightening the rows is part of the perfection of prayer.' And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Straighten your rows or Allah will cause discord among your hearts' - which refers to difference in hearts. And it is recommended for the imam to stand in front of the middle (of the row); if he does not, he has done wrong. And they should complete the first row, until if there is a gap in it but not in the second, one may break through the second row, because they have no sanctity due to their negligence in not filling the first row. Then complete the next, and so on. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Set up the rows, align the shoulders, fill the gaps, and be flexible with the hands of your brothers. Do not leave gaps for the devil. Whoever connects a row, Allah will connect him; whoever cuts a row, Allah will cut him.' And he said: 'The best of you are the most flexible of shoulders in prayer.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings regarding women's congregation prayer and the positioning of followers relative to the imam. The text begins by stating that women's congregation in prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), based on the hadith that a woman's prayer is best in her most private space. Their congregation involves the imam standing in their midst, which entails a prohibited element (the imam not being in front). If they do pray in congregation despite the dislike, the imam must stand in the middle of their row, like the imam of naked people, to minimize exposure. The commentator notes that this ruling is analogized from the congregation of naked persons, which is also prohibitively disliked due to either abandoning the wajib of being forward or increasing exposure. Then the text addresses the positioning of male followers: one male follower stands on the imam's right, level with him; two stand behind him. This is based on Prophetic practice. There is a difference reported from Abu Yusuf that the imam stands between the two followers, but the preferred view (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that they stand behind. The reasoning is that Ibn Mas'ud's practice (standing between them) was due to narrow space, whereas the Prophet's practice is the established sunna. The text also clarifies that a woman is considered nonexistent in the arrangement of rows, so if there is one man and one woman, the man stands beside the imam as if the woman weren't there. If there are many, the imam standing in their middle is prohibitively disliked because it abandons the wajib of being forward. Finally, the text covers the arrangement of rows: men's row first, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women, based on the hadith about mature people being nearest. It includes instructions for straightening rows, filling gaps, and the imam's position facing the middle of the row. The commentary emphasizes that all these rulings aim to maintain the order and dignity of congregational prayer.

Key Terms
جماعة النساء (jama'at al-nisa'): Women praying in congregation with a female imam or among themselves.
العراة (al-'urat): Naked persons, i.e., those without clothing. Their congregation is analogized to women's congregation regarding the imam's position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, women's congregation is:
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahrimi
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation is makruh tahrimi; if held, the imam stands in the middle.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Positioning of Followers in Congregational Prayer
Ruling with proof for follower positioning and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for positioning of one and two male followers and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding two followers.

Core Idea
One follower stands on the imam's right, two behind; the Hanafi school prefers the Prophetic practice over Ibn Mas'ud's due to spatial constraint.

This lesson delves into the proper arrangement of followers in congregational prayer. The passage not only states the positions but also addresses an internal Hanafi difference over where two followers should stand. We will analyze the evidence and understand the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the rule for one follower
Identify that one male follower stands on the imam's right, level with him, not behind. This is sunnah.
The text says 'on his right' is a condition of virtue.
2
State the rule for two followers
Two male followers stand behind the imam, not on either side.
This is the preferred view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf holds that the imam stands between the two followers. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The text presents both views.
4
Analyze the dalils
The Prophetic hadith (Anas and orphan behind) vs. Ibn Mas'ud's action (imam between). The text explains that Ibn Mas'ud's practice was due to narrow space, as reported by al-Nakha'i.
The Prophet's practice is preferred.
5
Understand the effect of women in rows
A woman is considered nonexistent in the arrangement, so if there is one man and one woman, the man stands beside the imam as if the woman were not there.
This is a unique Hanafi ruling.

Source Text

(فتح) فإن فعلن أي فإن أردن أن يصلين بجماعة (ط) وسطهن أي إن صلين بالجماعة مع كراهتها تقف الإمام وسطهن؛ لأن عائشة مهما فعلت كذلك، وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الإسلام ولأن في التقديم زيادة الكشف، ولا بد من تقدم عقب الإمام عن عقب من خلفها. Order of Rows and Etiquette in Congregational Prayer
Rules for row arrangement and etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of rows in congregational prayer and explain the sunna of straightening rows.

Core Idea
Rows are arranged by precedence: men, boys, hermaphrodites, women; straightening rows is part of the perfection of prayer.

This passage addresses the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer, including the order of different categories of people and the etiquettes of standing. These instructions ensure the congregation is orderly and spiritually optimal.

Guided Path
1
State the order of rows
From front to back: men, then boys, then hermaphrodites (khunatha), then women. This is based on the hadith 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible be nearest to me.'
This order prioritizes those with more responsibility and understanding.
2
Identify the ruling for imam's position
The imam should stand in front of the middle of the row; if not, he does wrong.
This is a sunna, not a wajib.
3
List the sunan of standing in rows
Stand shoulder to shoulder, fill gaps, align shoulders, be flexible with hands, and avoid leaving gaps for the devil.
These actions are part of the perfection of prayer.
4
Understand the completion of rows
The first row should be completed before starting the second. If there is a gap in the first row, one may break through the second row to fill it.
This emphasizes the importance of the first row.
5
Note the warnings and encouragements
Connecting a row brings Allah's connection; cutting a row brings cutting. The best are those who are most flexible in shoulders.
These are spiritual incentives.

Source Text

(فتح) فإن فعلن أي فإن أردن أن يصلين بجماعة (ط) وسطهن أي إن صلين بالجماعة مع كراهتها تقف الإمام وسطهن؛ لأن عائشة مهما فعلت كذلك، وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الإسلام ولأن في التقديم زيادة الكشف، ولا بد من تقدم عقب الإمام عن عقب من خلفها. (فتح، مستخلص) كالعراة: [ أي كما يقف إمام العراة وسطهم تحرزاً عن زيادة الكشف (ط)] جمع عار من الثوب، وفيه إيماء إلى كراهة جماعة العراة أيضاً كراهة تحريم؛ لاتحاد اللازم، وهو إما ترك واجب التقدم، أو زيادة الكشف. (فتح) ويقف الواحد إلخ ولو صبياً يعقل عنه يمينه بلا فرجة؛ لأنه عليها صلى بابن عباس هما فأقامه عن يمينه، وعن محمد أنه يضع أصابعه عند عقب الإمام، والعبرة لموضع الوقوف لا لموضع السجود حتى لو كان المقتدي أطول من الإمام فوقع سجوده أمام الإمام لم يضره، وقوله: "عن يمينه" قيد للفضيلة حتى لو صلى في يساره أو خلفه جاز ويكون مسيئاً لمخالفة السنة. [ رمز الحقائق: ٦٦/١] يمينه : أي المقتدي الواحد عن يمين الإمام مساوياً له لا متأخر عنه . (ط، ع) والاثنان خلفه وعن أبي يوسف أنه يتوسطهما؛ لأن ابن مسعود لما صلى بعلقمة والأسود في بيته وقام وسطهما، ولهما: أنه عليه صلى بأنس ويتيم فأقامهما خلفه وأم سليم وراءهما، وفعل ابن مسعود ما كان لضيق المقام، كذا قال النخعي، وهو أعلم الناس مذهب ابن مسعود والمرأة في حكم الاصطفاف كالعدم حتى لو كان خلفه رجل واحد وامرأة يقوم الرجل بحذائه كما لو لم يكن امرأة، وإن كثر القوم كره قيام الإمام وسطهم تحريماً لترك الواجب أي التقدم [ رمز الحقائق: ٦٦/١] (فتح) ويصف الرجال: أي صف الرجال مقدم على صف الصبيان وهو مقدم على صف الخناثي، وهو مقدم على صف النساء؛ لقوله : "ليلني منكم أولو الأحلام والنهى". [ تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٠/١] وينبغي للقوم أن يتراصوا ويسدوا الخلل ويسووا بين مناكبهم في الصفوف، ولا بأس أن يأمرهم الإمام بذلك لقوله عليه: "سووا صفوفكم؛ فإن تسوية الصفوف من تمام الصلاة"، وقال علي: لتسون صفوفكم أو ليخالفن الله بين وجوهكم" وهو راجع إلى اختلاف القلوب، وينبغي للإمام أن يقف بإزاء الوسط فإن لم يفعل فقد أساء، وينبغي أن يكملوا الصف الأول حتى إذا وجد فرجة فيه دون الثاني له أن يخرق الثاني؛ إذ لا حرمة لهم لتقصيرهم حيث لم يسدوا الصف الأول ثم يكمل ما يليه، وهلم جرا ، قال : "أقيموا الصفوف وحاذوا بين المناكب وسدوا الخلل ولينوا بأيدي إخوانكم ولا تذروا فرجات الشيطان من وصل صفاً وصله الله ومن قطع صفا قطعه الله"، وقال: "خياركم ألينكم مناكب في الصلاة". (فتح)
And (the chapter of) the congregation of women. If they do it, the imam stands in their middle like (the imam of) the naked. And one (follower) stands on his right, and two behind him, and the men arrange in rows. - Meaning it is also prohibitively disliked for them (to gather) alone? (?) The imam and the congregation of women: due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her courtyard, and her prayer in her private chamber is better than her prayer in her house.' And because their congregation alone involves committing a forbidden act, which is the imam standing in the middle of the row. (Fath) If they do it: meaning if they want to pray in congregation (T) in their middle: i.e., if they pray in congregation despite its dislike, the imam stands in their middle, because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did so, and her action is interpreted as in early Islam. And because putting him in front increases exposure. And the imam's heel must be ahead of the heels of those behind her. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Like the naked: (meaning just as the imam of the naked stands in their middle to avoid increased exposure - T) a plural of 'aryan (naked). And it implies that the congregation of the naked is also prohibitively disliked, because the same necessary consequence applies, which is either leaving the obligatory forward position or increasing exposure. (Fath) And one (follower) stands etc., even if a discerning boy, on his right without a gap; because he (peace be upon him) prayed with Ibn Abbas (?) and placed him on his right. And from Muhammad (ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani) that he places his fingers at the level of the imam's heel. And the consideration is for the place of standing, not the place of prostration; even if the follower is taller than the imam and his prostration occurs in front of the imam, it does not harm him. And his saying: 'on his right' is a condition of virtue; even if he prays on his left or behind him, it is permissible but he is doing wrong by violating the sunna. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/66] His right: meaning the individual follower stands on the right of the imam, level with him, not behind him. (T, A) And two behind him: And from Abu Yusuf that he (the imam) stands between them, because Ibn Mas'ud prayed with Alqama and al-Aswad in his house and stood between them. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that he (peace be upon him) prayed with Anas and an orphan and placed them behind him, and Umm Sulaym behind them. And Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to narrowness of space, as al-Nakha'i said, and he is the most knowledgeable of the people regarding Ibn Mas'ud's school. And a woman is as if nonexistent in the ranks: even if behind him there is one man and one woman, the man stands parallel to him as if there were no woman. And if the people are many, it is prohibitively disliked for the imam to stand in their middle because of abandoning the wajib, i.e., being forward. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/66] (Fath) And the men arrange in rows: meaning the row of men precedes the row of boys, which precedes the row of hermaphrodites (khunatha), which precedes the row of women; due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible (ulu al-ahlam wal-nuha) be nearest to me.' [Tabyin al-Haqaiq: 1/350] And it is recommended for the people to stand shoulder to shoulder, fill the gaps, and align their shoulders in the rows. And it is fine for the imam to command them to do so, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Straighten your rows, for straightening the rows is part of the perfection of prayer.' And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Straighten your rows or Allah will cause discord among your hearts' - which refers to difference in hearts. And it is recommended for the imam to stand in front of the middle (of the row); if he does not, he has done wrong. And they should complete the first row, until if there is a gap in it but not in the second, one may break through the second row, because they have no sanctity due to their negligence in not filling the first row. Then complete the next, and so on. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Set up the rows, align the shoulders, fill the gaps, and be flexible with the hands of your brothers. Do not leave gaps for the devil. Whoever connects a row, Allah will connect him; whoever cuts a row, Allah will cut him.' And he said: 'The best of you are the most flexible of shoulders in prayer.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings regarding women's congregation prayer and the positioning of followers relative to the imam. The text begins by stating that women's congregation in prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), based on the hadith that a woman's prayer is best in her most private space. Their congregation involves the imam standing in their midst, which entails a prohibited element (the imam not being in front). If they do pray in congregation despite the dislike, the imam must stand in the middle of their row, like the imam of naked people, to minimize exposure. The commentator notes that this ruling is analogized from the congregation of naked persons, which is also prohibitively disliked due to either abandoning the wajib of being forward or increasing exposure. Then the text addresses the positioning of male followers: one male follower stands on the imam's right, level with him; two stand behind him. This is based on Prophetic practice. There is a difference reported from Abu Yusuf that the imam stands between the two followers, but the preferred view (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that they stand behind. The reasoning is that Ibn Mas'ud's practice (standing between them) was due to narrow space, whereas the Prophet's practice is the established sunna. The text also clarifies that a woman is considered nonexistent in the arrangement of rows, so if there is one man and one woman, the man stands beside the imam as if the woman weren't there. If there are many, the imam standing in their middle is prohibitively disliked because it abandons the wajib of being forward. Finally, the text covers the arrangement of rows: men's row first, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women, based on the hadith about mature people being nearest. It includes instructions for straightening rows, filling gaps, and the imam's position facing the middle of the row. The commentary emphasizes that all these rulings aim to maintain the order and dignity of congregational prayer.

Key Terms
الصف الأول (al-saff al-awwal): The first row of congregational prayer, which holds the highest virtue.
تسوية الصفوف (taswiyat al-sufuf): The act of straightening rows, aligning shoulders, and filling gaps.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which group should form the first row in congregational prayer?
A) Boys
B) Men
C) Women
D) Khunatha

Key Takeaway
Rows are arranged in order: men, boys, khunatha, women; straightening and filling rows are sunna.

Ruling on Women's Congregation and Imam's Position
Explains ruling that women's congregation is makruh tahriman and imam stands in middle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregation (makruh tahrim) and explain the two proofs: the hadith on seclusion and the necessary consequence of the imam's position.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is makruh tahrim because it necessarily involves either omitting a wajib (imam ahead) or causing increased exposure.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on women praying in congregation without a male imam. You will learn why it is considered prohibitively disliked, based on a hadith emphasizing seclusion and a subtle juristic reasoning about the imam's placement. The passage also draws an analogy with the congregation of naked people.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is women praying in congregation without a male imam. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tahrim (prohibitively disliked).
Not haram, but sinful if done without necessity.
2
Locate the first dalil: Hadith
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than in her courtyard, and in her private chamber is better than in her house.' This indicates the virtue of seclusion.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but its meaning is clear.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The comparison 'better' shows that less secluded prayer is less virtuous. Since congregational prayer is less secluded than individual prayer at home, it is discouraged.
The hadith does not explicitly prohibit, but the implication is strong.
4
Identify the second dalil: Rational reasoning
If women pray alone, the imam must stand in their midst to avoid increased exposure. Standing in the middle contradicts the sunnah (imam ahead) – a necessary condition (wajib) is omitted, or exposure increases. Both are problematic.
This reasoning is based on the principle of sadd al-dhara'i.
5
Note the analogy with the naked
The ruling is similar to the congregation of naked people: the imam stands in the middle to minimize exposure, and the congregation is also makruh tahrim.
The analogy reinforces the underlying cause (illa) of avoiding exposure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجماعة النساء، فإن فعلن تقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة، أي كره تحريماً أيضاً وحدهن لقوله علي : صلاة المرأة في بيتها أفضل من صلاتها في حجرتها، وصلاتها في مخدعها أفضل من صلاتها في بيتها؛ ولأن جماعتهن وحدهن لا تخلو عن ارتكاب محرم، وهو وقوف الإمام وسط الصف. (فتح) فإن فعلن أي فإن أردن أن يصلين بجماعة (ط) وسطهن أي إن صلين بالجماعة مع كراهتها تقف الإمام وسطهن؛ لأن عائشة مهما فعلت كذلك، وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الإسلام ولأن في التقديم زيادة الكشف، ولا بد من تقدم عقب الإمام عن عقب من خلفها. (فتح، مستخلص) كالعراة: [ أي كما يقف إمام العراة وسطهم تحرزاً عن زيادة الكشف (ط)] جمع عار من الثوب، وفيه إيماء إلى كراهة جماعة العراة أيضاً كراهة تحريم؛ لاتحاد اللازم، وهو إما ترك واجب التقدم، أو زيادة الكشف. (فتح)
And the congregation of women, and if they do so, the imam stands in their midst like the naked. That is: it is also prohibited (tahriman) for them to be alone [in congregation], because of his statement (peace be upon him): A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her courtyard, and her prayer in her private chamber is better than her prayer in her house. And because their congregation alone is not free from committing a prohibited act, which is the imam standing in the middle of the row. (Fath) So if they do, meaning if they intend to pray in congregation (T), in their midst, meaning if they pray in congregation despite its dislike, the imam stands in their midst because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) used to do so; and her act of congregation is interpreted as in early Islam, and because putting him in front increases exposure, and it is necessary for the imam's heel to be ahead of the heel of those behind him. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Like the naked: that is, just as the imam of the naked stands in their midst to avoid increased exposure (T). 'Al-Arah' is plural of 'ari' (naked). This indicates that the congregation of the naked is also prohibited (tahriman) due to the same necessary consequence: either leaving the obligatory [act of] going forward, or increased exposure. (Fath)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on women praying in congregation. The text first states that women's congregation is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked). The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) that a woman's prayer in the innermost part of her house is better than in her courtyard, indicating the virtue of seclusion. The reason given is that women's congregation necessarily involves the imam standing in the middle of the row (to minimize exposure), which is a prohibited act (because it deviates from the sunnah of the imam standing ahead). The passage then explains that if women do choose to pray in congregation, the imam must stand in their midst, as Aisha (RA) did. This is justified by citing her practice, but it is considered abrogated or limited to early Islam. The analogy of the naked (al-uraat) is drawn: just as the imam of naked people stands in their midst to avoid exposure, so too for women. This indicates that even the congregation of naked men is also makruh tahriman due to the same necessary consequence: either the imam fails to stand ahead (a wajib) or there is increased exposure.

Key Terms
جماعة النساء (jama'at al-nisa'): Women praying in congregation among themselves without a male imam.
العراة (al-uraat): Naked people; used in analogy with women's congregation to highlight the same consequence of exposure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on women praying in congregation by themselves?
A) Mustahab
B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahrim
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation is makruh tahrim in the Hanafi school because it entails either omitting the sunnah position of the imam or increasing exposure, as supported by the hadith of seclusion and the analogy with the naked.

Positioning One or Two Followers Behind the Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's position for two followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah positioning for one and two followers and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam's placement when there are two followers.

Core Idea
One follower stands on the imam's right; two followers stand behind; the imam does not stand between them.

The proper arrangement of followers in congregational prayer is a sunnah that preserves order and follows the Prophet's practice. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains where one or two followers should stand and addresses a disagreement within the Hanafi school: should the imam stand between two followers or ahead of them? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh different proofs and recognize the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the default rule for one follower
Identify the ruling that a single follower (even a discerning boy) stands on the imam's right, level with him, not behind. This is sunnah muakkadah.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is the proof.
2
State the default rule for two followers
The matn says 'two behind him'. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn).
The hadith of Anas and the orphan is cited.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should stand between the two followers, based on the action of Ibn Mas'ud.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Evaluate the proofs
Compare the hadith used by the Sahibayn (explicit prophetic practice) with the companion action cited by Abu Yusuf. The commentary explains that Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to narrow space.
Al-Nakha'i, a student of Ibn Mas'ud, confirmed the narrow space reason.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the imam stands ahead and the two followers behind. Abu Yusuf's view is an exception for tight spaces.
This is the position taken in later fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف الواحد عن يمينه والاثنان خلفه ويقف الواحد إلخ ولو صبياً يعقل عنه يمينه بلا فرجة؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى بابن عباس فأقامه عن يمينه، وعن محمد أنه يضع أصابعه عند عقب الإمام، والعبرة لموضع الوقوف لا لموضع السجود حتى لو كان المقتدي أطول من الإمام فوقع سجوده أمام الإمام لم يضره، وقوله: "عن يمينه" قيد للفضيلة حتى لو صلى في يساره أو خلفه جاز ويكون مسيئاً لمخالفة السنة. يمينه : أي المقتدي الواحد عن يمين الإمام مساوياً له لا متأخر عنه. والاثنان خلفه وعن أبي يوسف أنه يتوسطهما؛ لأن ابن مسعود صلى بعلقمة والأسود في بيته وقام وسطهما، ولهما: أنه صلى بأنس ويتيم فأقامهما خلفه وأم سليم وراءهما، وفعل ابن مسعود ما كان لضيق المقام، والمرأة في حكم الاصطفاف كالعدم حتى لو كان خلفه رجل واحد وامرأة يقوم الرجل بحذائه كما لو لم يكن امرأة، وإن كثر القوم كره قيام الإمام وسطهم تحريماً لترك الواجب أي التقدم [ رمز الحقائق: ٦٦/١] (فتح)
And one stands on his right and two behind him. And the one stands ... even if a boy who understands, on his right without a gap; because he (peace be upon him) prayed with Ibn Abbas and placed him on his right, and from Muhammad that he places his fingers at the imam's heel, and the consideration is the place of standing not the place of prostration, so if the follower is taller than the imam and his prostration occurs in front of the imam, it does not harm him. His statement 'on his right' is a restriction for virtue, so if he prays on his left or behind him, it is permissible but he is doing wrong by opposing the sunnah. 'His right' means the single follower is on the imam's right, level with him, not behind him. And two are behind him, and from Abu Yusuf that he (the imam) stands between them; because Ibn Mas'ud prayed with 'Alqama and al-Aswad in his house and stood between them, and for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that he (peace be upon him) prayed with Anas and a orphan and placed them behind him and Umm Sulaym behind them, and Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to tight space. And a woman is like non-existent in the ruling of row arrangement, so if there is one man and a woman behind him, the man stands alongside him as if there were no woman. And if the people are many, it is prohibitively disliked for the imam to stand in their midst due to leaving the wajib (i.e., being ahead). [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 1/66] (Fath)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses the proper positioning of followers relative to the imam. The matn states that one follower stands on the imam's right, and two followers stand behind him. The commentary expands by noting that even a discerning boy may stand on the right without a gap. The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who placed Ibn Abbas on his right. There is a transmission from Imam Muhammad that the follower aligns his toes with the imam's heels. The virtue and ruling are distinguished: it is sunnah to stand on the right, but if one stands on the left or directly behind, the prayer is valid but disliked. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should stand in between the two followers (i.e., in the middle of the row), based on the action of Ibn Mas'ud. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on the hadith of Anas and the orphan, showing the imam stands ahead. The passage reconciles this by noting that Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to a narrow space. Finally, the ruling on women is that they are considered non-existent for row arrangement; a single man with one woman still stands alone behind the imam as if no woman were present. The imam standing in the middle of a large group is prohibitively disliked because it abandons the wajib of being ahead.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in prayer, also called al-ma'mum.
عقب الإمام (aqib al-imam): The heel of the imam; used as a point of alignment for placement of followers' toes.
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahririyyah): Prohibitively disliked; closer to haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, where should two followers stand in relation to the imam?
A) One on each side of the imam
B) Behind the imam
C) One behind and one to the right
D) In front of the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that two followers stand behind the imam; the imam standing between them is only permissible in narrow spaces.
